1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Sound-icon.svg/40px-Sound-icon.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></div>\n</div>\n<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">British Empire</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">\n<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/w/index.php?title=British_empire&amp;redirect=no" title="British empire">British empire</a>)</span></div>\n<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">States and dominions ruled by the United Kingdom</div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n<table class="infobox geography vcard" style="width:22em;font-size:88%;"><tbody><tr><th class="adr" colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;padding:0.25em 0.33em 0.33em;line-height:1.2em;font-size:1.25em;"><div style="padding-top:0.25em; font-weight:normal;"><div class="fn org country-name" style="display:inline"><b>British Empire</b></div></div></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align:center;padding:0.5em 0;"><div style="padding: 0px 5px;">\n<div style="padding-bottom:3px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg" title="Flag of the United Kingdom of British Empire"><img alt="Flag of the United Kingdom of British Empire" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="63" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/125px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/188px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/250px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" width="125"/></a></div>\n<div style="font-size:90%;"><a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Flag of the United Kingdom">Flag of the United Kingdom</a></div>\n</div></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_British_Empire.png" title="All areas of the world that were ever part of the British Empire. Current British Overseas Territories have their names underlined in red."><img alt="All areas of the world that were ever part of the British Empire. Current British Overseas Territories have their names underlined in red." data-file-height="1400" data-file-width="2753" decoding="async" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/The_British_Empire.png/250px-The_British_Empire.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/The_British_Empire.png/375px-The_British_Empire.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/The_British_Empire.png/500px-The_British_Empire.png 2x" width="250"/></a><div style="font-size:90%;position:relative;top:0.3em;">All areas of the world that were ever part of the British Empire. Current <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territories</a> have their names underlined in red.</div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>British Empire</b> comprised the <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">dominions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">colonies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorates</a>, <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">mandates</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Dependent_territory" title="Dependent territory">territories</a> ruled or administered by the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> and its predecessor states. It originated with the <a href="/wiki/English_overseas_possessions" title="English overseas possessions">overseas possessions</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trading_post" title="Trading post">trading posts</a> established by <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">England</a> between the late 16th and early 18th centuries. At its height, it was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_empires" title="List of largest empires">largest empire in history</a> and, for over a century, was the foremost <a href="/wiki/Power_(international_relations)#Categories_of_power" title="Power (international relations)">global power</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b-1">[1]</a></sup> By 1913, the British Empire held sway over 412 million people, <span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7001230000000000000&#9824;</span>23% of the world population at the time,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> and by 1920, it covered 35,500,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (13,700,000&#160;sq&#160;mi),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> <span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7001240000000000000&#9824;</span>24% of the Earth\'s total land area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> As a result, its political, <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">legal</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">linguistic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Culture of the United Kingdom">cultural</a> legacy is widespread. At the peak of its power, the phrase "<a href="/wiki/The_empire_on_which_the_sun_never_sets" title="The empire on which the sun never sets">the empire on which the sun never sets</a>" was often used to describe the British Empire, because its expanse around the globe meant that the sun was always shining on at least one of its territories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a> in the 15th and 16th centuries, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portugal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spain</a> pioneered European exploration of the globe, and in the process established large overseas empires. Envious of the great wealth these empires generated,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> England, <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">France</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Netherlands</a> began to establish colonies and trade networks of their own in the Americas and Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b3_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b3-7">[7]</a></sup> A series of wars in the 17th and 18th centuries with the Netherlands and France left England and then, following <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">union between England and Scotland</a> in 1707, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a>, the dominant <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonial power</a> in North America. It then became the dominant power in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a> after the <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a>\'s conquest of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mughal_Bengal" title="Mughal Bengal">Mughal Bengal</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Plassey" title="Battle of Plassey">Battle of Plassey</a> in 1757.\n</p><p>The independence of the <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a> in North America in 1783 after the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American War of Independence</a> caused Britain to lose some of its oldest and most populous colonies. British attention soon turned towards Asia, Africa, and the Pacific. After the defeat of France in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_revolutionary_wars" title="French revolutionary wars">Revolutionary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a> (1792&#8211;1815), Britain emerged as the principal naval and imperial power of the 19th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy#1815&#8211;1914" title="Royal Navy">Unchallenged at sea</a>, British dominance was later described as <i><a href="/wiki/Pax_Britannica" title="Pax Britannica">Pax Britannica</a></i> ("British Peace"), a period of relative peace in Europe and the world (1815&#8211;1914) during which the British Empire became the global <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hegemon" title="Hegemon">hegemon</a> and adopted the role of global policeman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> In the early 19th century, the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> began to transform Britain; so that by the time of <a href="/wiki/The_Great_Exhibition" title="The Great Exhibition">the Great Exhibition</a> in 1851, the country was described as the "workshop of the world".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The British Empire expanded to include <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">most of India</a>, large <a href="/wiki/British_Empire#Cape_to_Cairo" title="British Empire">parts of Africa</a> and many other territories throughout the world. Alongside the formal control that Britain exerted over its own colonies, its dominance of much of world trade meant that it effectively <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Informal_Empire" title="Informal Empire">controlled the economies of many regions</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the 19th century, Britain\'s population increased at a dramatic rate, accompanied by rapid urbanisation, which caused significant social and economic stresses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> To seek new markets and sources of raw materials, the British government under <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Disraeli" title="Benjamin Disraeli">Benjamin Disraeli</a> initiated a period of imperial expansion in Egypt, South Africa, and elsewhere. Canada, Australia, and New Zealand became self-governing dominions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the start of the 20th century, <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">Germany</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> had begun to challenge Britain\'s economic lead. Subsequent military and economic tensions between Britain and Germany were major causes of the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a>, during which Britain relied heavily upon its empire. The conflict placed enormous strain on the military, financial and manpower resources of Britain. Although the British Empire achieved its largest territorial extent immediately after World War I, Britain was no longer the world\'s pre-eminent industrial or military power. In the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>, Britain\'s colonies in <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> were occupied by <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japan</a>. Despite the final victory of Britain and its allies, the damage to British prestige helped to accelerate the decline of the empire. India, Britain\'s most valuable and populous possession, achieved <a href="/wiki/Indian_independence_movement" title="Indian independence movement">independence</a> as part of a larger <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decolonisation" title="Decolonisation">decolonisation</a> movement in which Britain granted independence to most territories of the empire. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transfer_of_sovereignty_over_Hong_Kong" title="Transfer of sovereignty over Hong Kong">transfer of Hong Kong to China</a> in 1997 marked for many the end of the British Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brendon-Empire-end_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brendon-Empire-end-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prince-Charles-Empire-End_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Prince-Charles-Empire-End-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refohbev594_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-refohbev594-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC-Empire-End_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-Empire-End-20">[20]</a></sup> Fourteen <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">overseas territories</a> remain under British sovereignty.\n</p><p>After independence, many former British colonies joined the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, a free association of independent states. The United Kingdom is now one of 16 Commonwealth nations, a grouping known informally as the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realms</a>, that share a <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Monarchy of the United Kingdom">monarch</a>, currently Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span <span class="toctext">Americas, Africa and the slave trade</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#Rivalry_with_the_Netherlands_in_Asia"><span class="tocnumber">2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Rivalry with the Netherlands in Asia</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#Global_conflicts_with_France"><span class="tocnumber">2.3</span> <span class="toctext">Global conflicts with France</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7"><a href="#Loss_of_the_Thirteen_American_Colonies"><span class="tocnumber">2.4</span> <span class="toctext">Loss of the Thirteen American Colonies</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href=\'#Rise_of_the_"Second"_British_Empire_(1783&#8211;1815)\'><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Rise of the "Second" British Empire (1783&#8211;1815)</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Exploration_of_the_Pacific"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Exploration of the Pacific</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#War_with_Napoleonic_France"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">War with Napoleonic France</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#Abolition_of_slavery"><span class="tocnumber">3.3</span> <span class="toctext">Abolition of slavery</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Britain\'s_imperial_century_(1815&#8211;1914)"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Britain\'s imperial century (1815&#8211;1914)</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#East_India_Company_in_Asia"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">East India Company in Asia</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Rivalry_with_Russia"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Rivalry with Russia</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Cape_to_Cairo"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Cape to Cairo</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Changing_status_of_the_white_colonies"><span class="tocnumber">4.4</span> <span class="toctext">Changing status of the white colonies</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#World_wars_(1914&#8211;1945)"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">World wars (1914&#8211;1945)</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#First_World_War"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">First World War</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Inter-war_period"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Inter-war period</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Second_World_War"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Second World War</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Decolonisation_and_decline_(1945&#8211;1997)"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Decolonisation and decline (1945&#8211;1997)</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Initial_disengagement"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Initial disengagement</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Suez_and_its_aftermath"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Suez and its aftermath</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Wind_of_change"><span class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext">Wind of change</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#End_of_empire"><span class="tocnumber">6.4</span> <span class="toctext">End of empire</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#Legacy"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Legacy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span id="Origins_.281497.E2.80.931583.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins_(1497&#8211;1583)">Origins (1497&#8211;1583)</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Matthew-BristolHarbour-Aug2004.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="764" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Matthew-BristolHarbour-Aug2004.jpg/170px-Matthew-BristolHarbour-Aug2004.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Matthew-BristolHarbour-Aug2004.jpg/255px-Matthew-BristolHarbour-Aug2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Matthew-BristolHarbour-Aug2004.jpg/340px-Matthew-BristolHarbour-Aug2004.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Matthew-BristolHarbour-Aug2004.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A replica of the <i><a href="/wiki/Matthew_(ship)" title="Matthew (ship)">Matthew</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/John_Cabot" title="John Cabot">John Cabot</a>\'s ship used for his second voyage to the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The foundations of the British Empire were laid when <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland" title="Kingdom of Scotland">Scotland</a> were separate kingdoms. In 1496, King <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">Henry VII of England</a>, following the successes of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portugal</a> in overseas exploration, commissioned <a href="/wiki/John_Cabot" title="John Cabot">John Cabot</a> to lead a voyage to discover a route to Asia via the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">North Atlantic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b3_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b3-7">[7]</a></sup> Cabot sailed in 1497, five years after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_discovery_of_America" title="European discovery of America">European discovery of America</a>, but he made landfall on the coast of <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a>, and, mistakenly believing (like <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>) that he had reached Asia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> there was no attempt to found a colony. Cabot led another voyage to the Americas the following year but nothing was ever heard of his ships again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b4_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b4-22">[22]</a></sup>\n</p><p>No further attempts to establish English colonies in the Americas were made until well into the reign of Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_I_of_England" title="Elizabeth I of England">Elizabeth I</a>, during the last decades of the 16th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> In the meantime, the 1533 <a href="/wiki/Statute_in_Restraint_of_Appeals" title="Statute in Restraint of Appeals">Statute in Restraint of Appeals</a> had declared "that this realm of England is an Empire".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The subsequent <a href="/wiki/English_Reformation" title="English Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a> turned England and <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a> Spain into implacable enemies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b3_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b3-7">[7]</a></sup> In 1562, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_monarchs" title="List of English monarchs">English Crown</a> encouraged the <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">privateers</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Hawkins_(naval_commander)" title="John Hawkins (naval commander)">John Hawkins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francis_Drake" title="Francis Drake">Francis Drake</a> to engage in slave-raiding attacks against Spanish and Portuguese ships off the coast of West Africa<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> with the aim of breaking into the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a>. This effort was rebuffed and later, as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglo-Spanish_War_(1585)" title="Anglo-Spanish War (1585)">Anglo-Spanish Wars</a> intensified, Elizabeth I gave her blessing to further privateering raids against Spanish ports in the Americas and shipping that was returning across the Atlantic, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_treasure_fleet" title="Spanish treasure fleet">laden with treasure</a> from the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b7_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b7-26">[26]</a></sup> At the same time, influential writers such as <a href="/wiki/Richard_Hakluyt" title="Richard Hakluyt">Richard Hakluyt</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Dee" title="John Dee">John Dee</a> (who was the first to use the term "British Empire")<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> were beginning to press for the establishment of England\'s own empire. By this time, Spain had become the dominant power in the Americas and was exploring the Pacific Ocean, Portugal had established trading posts and forts from the coasts of Africa and <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> to China, and <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">France</a> had begun to settle the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_River" title="Saint Lawrence River">Saint Lawrence River</a> area, later to become <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plantations_of_Ireland">Plantations of Ireland</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Plantations_of_Ireland" title="Plantations of Ireland">Plantations of Ireland</a></div>\n<p>Although England trailed behind other European powers in establishing overseas colonies, it had been engaged during the 16th century in the settlement of Ireland with Protestants from England and Scotland, drawing on precedents dating back to the <a href="/wiki/Norman_invasion_of_Ireland" title="Norman invasion of Ireland">Norman invasion of Ireland</a> in 1169.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Several people who helped establish the Plantations of Ireland also played a part in the early colonisation of North America, particularly a group known as the <a href="/wiki/West_Country_men" title="West Country men">West Country men</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id=".22First.22_British_Empire_.281583.E2.80.931783.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id=\'"First"_British_Empire_(1583&#8211;1783)\'>"First" British Empire (1583&#8211;1783)</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/English_overseas_possessions" title="English overseas possessions">English overseas possessions</a></div>\n<p>In 1578, Elizabeth I granted a patent to <a href="/wiki/Humphrey_Gilbert" title="Humphrey Gilbert">Humphrey Gilbert</a> for discovery and overseas exploration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> That year, Gilbert sailed for the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> with the intention of engaging in <a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">piracy</a> and establishing a colony in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>, but the expedition was aborted before it had crossed the Atlantic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> In 1583, he embarked on a second attempt, on this occasion to the island of <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a> whose harbour he formally claimed for England, although no settlers were left behind. Gilbert did not survive the return journey to England, and was succeeded by his half-brother, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Raleigh" title="Walter Raleigh">Walter Raleigh</a>, who was granted his own patent by Elizabeth in 1584. Later that year, Raleigh founded the <a href="/wiki/Roanoke_Colony" title="Roanoke Colony">Roanoke Colony</a> on the coast of present-day <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>, but lack of supplies caused the colony to fail.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1603, <a href="/wiki/James_VI_and_I" title="James VI and I">James VI, King of Scots</a>, ascended (as James I) to the English throne and in 1604 negotiated the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_London_(1604)" title="Treaty of London (1604)">Treaty of London</a>, ending hostilities with <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spain</a>. Now at peace with its main rival, English attention shifted from preying on other nations\' colonial infrastructures to the business of establishing its own overseas colonies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The British Empire began to take shape during the early 17th century, with the <a href="/wiki/British_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="British colonization of the Americas">English settlement</a> of North America and the smaller islands of the Caribbean, and the establishment of <a href="/wiki/Joint-stock_company" title="Joint-stock company">joint-stock companies</a>, most notably the <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a>, to administer colonies and overseas trade. This period, until the loss of the <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a> after the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American War of Independence</a> towards the end of the 18th century, has subsequently been referred to by some historians as the "First British Empire".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Americas.2C_Africa_and_the_slave_trade"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Americas,_Africa_and_the_slave_trade">Americas, Africa and the slave trade</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_colonisation_of_the_Americas" title="British colonisation of the Americas">British colonisation of the Americas</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_America" title="British America">British America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> initially provided England\'s most important and lucrative colonies,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> but not before several attempts at colonisation failed. An attempt to establish a colony in <a href="/wiki/British_Guiana" title="British Guiana">Guiana</a> in 1604 lasted only two years, and failed in its main objective to find gold deposits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Colonies in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">St Lucia</a>&#160;(1605) and <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a>&#160;(1609) also rapidly folded, but settlements were successfully established in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts" title="Saint Kitts">St. Kitts</a>&#160;(1624), <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>&#160;(1627) and <a href="/wiki/Nevis" title="Nevis">Nevis</a>&#160;(1628).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> The colonies soon adopted the system of <a href="/wiki/Plantation" title="Plantation">sugar plantations</a> successfully used by the Portuguese in <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Brazil" title="Colonial Brazil">Brazil</a>, which depended on slave labour, and&#8212;at first&#8212;Dutch ships, to sell the slaves and buy the sugar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> To ensure that the increasingly healthy profits of this trade remained in English hands, Parliament <a href="/wiki/Navigation_Acts" title="Navigation Acts">decreed</a> in 1651 that only English ships would be able to ply their trade in English colonies. This led to hostilities with the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">United Dutch Provinces</a>&#8212;a series of <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Dutch_Wars" title="Anglo-Dutch Wars">Anglo-Dutch Wars</a>&#8212;which would eventually strengthen England\'s position in the Americas at the expense of the Dutch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> In 1655, England annexed the island of <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> from the Spanish, and in 1666 succeeded in colonising the <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">Bahamas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:British_America.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="329" data-file-width="383" decoding="async" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/British_America.png/220px-British_America.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/British_America.png/330px-British_America.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/75/British_America.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:British_America.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>British colonies in North America, 1763&#8211;1776</div></div></div>\n<p>England\'s first permanent settlement in the Americas was founded in 1607 in <a href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Virginia" title="Jamestown, Virginia">Jamestown</a>, led by Captain <a href="/wiki/John_Smith_(explorer)" title="John Smith (explorer)">John Smith</a> and managed by the <a href="/wiki/London_Company" title="London Company">Virginia Company</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a> was settled and claimed by England as a result of the 1609 shipwreck of the Virginia Company\'s <a href="/wiki/Sea_Venture" title="Sea Venture">flagship</a>, and in 1615 was turned over to the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Somers_Isles_Company" title="Somers Isles Company">Somers Isles Company</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> The Virginia Company\'s charter was revoked in 1624 and direct control of Virginia was assumed by the <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">crown</a>, thereby founding the <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Virginia" title="Colony of Virginia">Colony of Virginia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/London_and_Bristol_Company" title="London and Bristol Company">London and Bristol Company</a> was created in 1610 with the aim of creating a permanent settlement on Newfoundland, but was largely unsuccessful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> In 1620, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Colony" title="Plymouth Colony">Plymouth</a> was founded as a haven for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puritan" title="Puritan">Puritan</a> religious separatists, later known as the <a href="/wiki/Pilgrim" title="Pilgrim">Pilgrims</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Fleeing from <a href="/wiki/Religious_persecution" title="Religious persecution">religious persecution</a> would become the motive of many English would-be colonists to risk the arduous <a href="/wiki/Transatlantic_crossing" title="Transatlantic crossing">trans-Atlantic voyage</a>: <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Maryland" title="Province of Maryland">Maryland</a> was founded as a haven for <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholics</a>&#160;(1634), <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Rhode_Island_and_Providence_Plantations" title="Colony of Rhode Island and Providence Plantations">Rhode Island</a>&#160;(1636) as a colony tolerant of all religions and Connecticut&#160;(1639) for <a href="/wiki/Congregational_church" title="Congregational church">Congregationalists</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Carolina" title="Province of Carolina">Province of Carolina</a> was founded in 1663. With the surrender of <a href="/wiki/Fort_Amsterdam" title="Fort Amsterdam">Fort Amsterdam</a> in 1664, England gained control of the Dutch colony of <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">New Netherland</a>, renaming it New York. This was formalised in negotiations following the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Dutch_Wars" title="Anglo-Dutch Wars">Second Anglo-Dutch War</a>, in exchange for <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> In 1681, the colony of <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Pennsylvania" title="Province of Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a> was founded by <a href="/wiki/William_Penn" title="William Penn">William Penn</a>. The American colonies were less financially successful than those of the Caribbean, but had large areas of good agricultural land and attracted far larger numbers of English emigrants who preferred their temperate climates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b72&#8211;73_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b72&#8211;73-49">[49]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tobacco_cultivation_(Virginia,_ca._1670).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="411" data-file-width="794" decoding="async" height="114" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Tobacco_cultivation_%28Virginia%2C_ca._1670%29.jpg/220px-Tobacco_cultivation_%28Virginia%2C_ca._1670%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Tobacco_cultivation_%28Virginia%2C_ca._1670%29.jpg/330px-Tobacco_cultivation_%28Virginia%2C_ca._1670%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Tobacco_cultivation_%28Virginia%2C_ca._1670%29.jpg/440px-Tobacco_cultivation_%28Virginia%2C_ca._1670%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tobacco_cultivation_(Virginia,_ca._1670).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>African slaves working in 17th-century <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Virginia" title="Colony of Virginia">Virginia</a>, by an unknown artist, 1670</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1670, <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles II</a> incorporated by <a href="/wiki/Royal_charter" title="Royal charter">royal charter</a> the <a href="/wiki/Hudson%27s_Bay_Company" title="Hudson\'s Bay Company">Hudson\'s Bay Company</a> (HBC), granting it a monopoly on the <a href="/wiki/North_American_fur_trade" title="North American fur trade">fur trade</a> in the area known as <a href="/wiki/Rupert%27s_Land" title="Rupert\'s Land">Rupert\'s Land</a>, which would later form a large proportion of the <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Dominion of Canada</a>. Forts and trading posts established by the HBC were frequently the subject of attacks by the French, who had established their own fur trading colony in adjacent <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-buckner25_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-buckner25-50">[50]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Two years later, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_African_Company" title="Royal African Company">Royal African Company</a> was inaugurated, receiving from King Charles a monopoly of the trade to supply slaves to the British colonies of the Caribbean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> From the outset, <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slavery</a> was the basis of the British Empire in the West Indies. Until the abolition of its slave trade in 1807, Britain was responsible for the transportation of 3.5 million African slaves to the Americas, a third of all <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">slaves transported across the Atlantic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b62_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b62-52">[52]</a></sup> To facilitate this trade, forts were established on the coast of West Africa, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Island_(The_Gambia)" title="James Island (The Gambia)">James Island</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Ghana" title="Jamestown, Ghana">Accra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bunce_Island" title="Bunce Island">Bunce Island</a>. In the British Caribbean, the percentage of the population of African descent rose from 25% in 1650 to around 80% in 1780, and in the Thirteen Colonies from 10% to 40% over the same period (the majority in the southern colonies).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> For the slave traders, the trade was extremely profitable, and became a major economic mainstay for such western <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">British cities</a> as <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>, which formed the third corner of the <a href="/wiki/Triangular_trade" title="Triangular trade">triangular trade</a> with Africa and the Americas. For the transported, harsh and unhygienic conditions on the slaving ships and poor diets meant that the average <a href="/wiki/Mortality_rate" title="Mortality rate">mortality rate</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Passage" title="Middle Passage">Middle Passage</a> was one in seven.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1695, the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Scotland" title="Parliament of Scotland">Parliament of Scotland</a> granted a charter to the <a href="/wiki/Company_of_Scotland" title="Company of Scotland">Company of Scotland</a>, which established a settlement in 1698 on the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Panama" title="Isthmus of Panama">Isthmus of Panama</a>. Besieged by neighbouring Spanish colonists of <a href="/wiki/New_Kingdom_of_Granada" title="New Kingdom of Granada">New Granada</a>, and afflicted by <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>, the colony was abandoned two years later. The <a href="/wiki/Darien_scheme" title="Darien scheme">Darien scheme</a> was a financial disaster for Scotland&#8212;a quarter of Scottish capital<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> was lost in the enterprise&#8212;and ended Scottish hopes of establishing its own overseas empire. The episode also had major political consequences, persuading the governments of both England and Scotland of the merits of a union of countries, rather than just crowns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> This occurred in 1707 with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Union" title="Treaty of Union">Treaty of Union</a>, establishing the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalry_with_the_Netherlands_in_Asia">Rivalry with the Netherlands in Asia</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fort_St._George,_Chennai.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="826" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Fort_St._George%2C_Chennai.jpg/250px-Fort_St._George%2C_Chennai.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Fort_St._George%2C_Chennai.jpg/375px-Fort_St._George%2C_Chennai.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Fort_St._George%2C_Chennai.jpg/500px-Fort_St._George%2C_Chennai.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fort_St._George,_Chennai.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_St._George_(India)" title="Fort St. George (India)">Fort St. George</a> was founded at <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Madras</a> in 1639.</div></div></div>\n<p>At the end of the 16th century, England and the Netherlands began to challenge Portugal\'s monopoly of trade with Asia, forming private <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joint_stock_company" title="Joint stock company">joint-stock companies</a> to finance the voyages&#8212;the English, later British, <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a>, chartered in 1600 and 1602 respectively. The primary aim of these companies was to tap into the lucrative <a href="/wiki/Spice_trade" title="Spice trade">spice trade</a>, an effort focused mainly on two regions; the <a href="/wiki/Malay_Archipelago" title="Malay Archipelago">East Indies archipelago</a>, and an important hub in the trade network, India. There, they competed for trade supremacy with Portugal and with each other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Although England ultimately eclipsed the Netherlands as a colonial power, in the short term the Netherlands\' more advanced financial system<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b19_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b19-58">[58]</a></sup> and the three <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Dutch_Wars" title="Anglo-Dutch Wars">Anglo-Dutch Wars</a> of the 17th century left it with a stronger position in Asia. Hostilities ceased after the <a href="/wiki/Glorious_Revolution" title="Glorious Revolution">Glorious Revolution</a> of 1688 when the Dutch <a href="/wiki/William_III_of_England" title="William III of England">William of Orange</a> ascended the English throne, bringing peace between the Netherlands and England. A deal between the two nations left the spice trade of the East Indies archipelago to the Netherlands and the textiles industry of India to England, but textiles soon overtook spices in terms of profitability, and by 1720, in terms of sales, the British company had overtaken the Dutch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b19_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b19-58">[58]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_conflicts_with_France">Global conflicts with France</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Benjamin_West_005.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Benjamin_West_005.jpg/250px-Benjamin_West_005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Benjamin_West_005.jpg/375px-Benjamin_West_005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Benjamin_West_005.jpg/500px-Benjamin_West_005.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Benjamin_West_005.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The death of British General <a href="/wiki/James_Wolfe" title="James Wolfe">James Wolfe</a> at the 1759 <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Plains_of_Abraham" title="Battle of the Plains of Abraham">Battle of Quebec</a> during the <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">French and Indian War</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Peace between England and the Netherlands in 1688 meant that the two countries entered the <a href="/wiki/Nine_Years%27_War" title="Nine Years\' War">Nine Years\' War</a> as allies, but the conflict&#8212;waged in Europe and overseas between France, Spain and the Anglo-Dutch alliance&#8212;left the English a stronger colonial power than the Dutch, who were forced to devote a larger proportion of their <a href="/wiki/Military_budget" title="Military budget">military budget</a> on the costly land war in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> The 18th century saw England (<a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">after 1707, Britain</a>) rise to be the world\'s dominant colonial power, and France becoming its main rival on the imperial stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The death of <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_Spain" title="Charles II of Spain">Charles II of Spain</a> in 1700 and his bequeathal of Spain and its colonial empire to <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Spain" title="Philip V of Spain">Philippe of Anjou</a>, a grandson of the <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV_of_France" title="Louis XIV of France">King of France</a>, raised the prospect of the unification of France, Spain and their respective colonies, an unacceptable state of affairs for England and the other powers of Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shennan11_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-shennan11-61">[61]</a></sup> In 1701, England, Portugal and the Netherlands sided with the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> against Spain and France in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a>, which lasted until 1714.\n</p><p>At the concluding <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht" title="Treaty of Utrecht">Treaty of Utrecht</a>, Philip renounced his and his descendants\' right to the French throne and Spain lost its empire in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shennan11_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-shennan11-61">[61]</a></sup> The British Empire was territorially enlarged: from France, Britain gained <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Acadia" title="Acadia">Acadia</a>, and from Spain, <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Menorca" title="Menorca">Menorca</a>. Gibraltar became a critical naval base and allowed Britain to control the Atlantic entry and exit point to the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a>. Spain also ceded the rights to the lucrative <i><a href="/wiki/Asiento" title="Asiento">asiento</a></i> (permission to sell slaves in <a href="/wiki/Ibero-America" title="Ibero-America">Spanish America</a>) to Britain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Clive.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1870" data-file-width="2400" decoding="async" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Clive.jpg/250px-Clive.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Clive.jpg/375px-Clive.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Clive.jpg/500px-Clive.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Clive.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Robert_Clive" title="Robert Clive">Robert Clive</a>\'s victory at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Plassey" title="Battle of Plassey">Battle of Plassey</a> established the <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a> as a military as well as a commercial power.</div></div></div>\n<p>During the middle decades of the 18th century, there were several outbreaks of military conflict on the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Carnatic_Wars" title="Carnatic Wars">Carnatic Wars</a>, as the English East India Company (often known simply as "the Company") and its French counterpart, the <a href="/wiki/French_East_India_Company" title="French East India Company">French East India Company</a> (<i>Compagnie fran&#231;aise des Indes orientales</i>), struggled alongside local rulers to fill the vacuum that had been left by the decline of the <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal Empire</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Plassey" title="Battle of Plassey">Battle of Plassey</a> in 1757, in which the British, led by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Clive" title="Robert Clive">Robert Clive</a>, defeated the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nawab_of_Bengal" title="Nawab of Bengal">Nawab of Bengal</a> and his French allies, left the British East India Company in control of <a href="/wiki/Bengal" title="Bengal">Bengal</a> and as the major military and political power in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> France was left control of its <a href="/wiki/French_India" title="French India">enclaves</a> but with military restrictions and an obligation to support British <a href="/wiki/Client_state" title="Client state">client states</a>, ending French hopes of controlling India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> In the following decades the British East India Company gradually increased the size of the territories under its control, either ruling directly or via local rulers under the threat of force from the <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_Army" title="British Indian Army">British Indian Army</a>, the vast majority of which was composed of Indian <a href="/wiki/Sepoy" title="Sepoy">sepoys</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The British and French struggles in India became but one theatre of the global <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years\' War">Seven Years\' War</a> (1756&#8211;1763) involving France, Britain and the other major European powers. The signing of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Treaty of Paris (1763)</a> had important consequences for the future of the British Empire. In North America, France\'s future as a colonial power effectively ended with the recognition of British claims to <a href="/wiki/Rupert%27s_Land" title="Rupert\'s Land">Rupert\'s Land</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-buckner25_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-buckner25-50">[50]</a></sup> and the ceding of <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a> to Britain (leaving a sizeable <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Canadian" title="French Canadian">French-speaking population</a> under British control) and <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_(New_France)" title="Louisiana (New France)">Louisiana</a> to Spain. Spain ceded Florida to Britain. Along with its victory over France in India, the Seven Years\' War therefore left Britain as the world\'s most powerful maritime power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refpagden1_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-refpagden1-66">[66]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Loss_of_the_Thirteen_American_Colonies">Loss of the Thirteen American Colonies</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a></div>\n<p>During the 1760s and early 1770s, relations between the <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a> and Britain became increasingly strained, primarily because of resentment of the British Parliament\'s attempts to govern and tax American colonists without their consent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b84_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b84-67">[67]</a></sup> This was summarised at the time by the slogan "<a href="/wiki/No_taxation_without_representation" title="No taxation without representation">No taxation without representation</a>", a perceived violation of the guaranteed <a href="/wiki/Rights_of_Englishmen" title="Rights of Englishmen">Rights of Englishmen</a>. The <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a> began with rejection of Parliamentary authority and moves towards self-government. In response, Britain sent troops to reimpose direct rule, leading to the outbreak of <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">war</a> in 1775. The following year, in 1776, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">United States declared independence</a>. The entry of <a href="/wiki/France_in_the_American_Revolutionary_War" title="France in the American Revolutionary War">France</a> into the war in 1778 tipped the military balance in the Americans\' favour and after a decisive defeat at <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Yorktown" title="Siege of Yorktown">Yorktown</a> in 1781, Britain began negotiating peace terms. American independence was acknowledged at the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Peace of Paris (1783)">Peace of Paris</a> in 1783.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Surrender_of_Lord_Cornwallis.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1978" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Surrender_of_Lord_Cornwallis.jpg/220px-Surrender_of_Lord_Cornwallis.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Surrender_of_Lord_Cornwallis.jpg/330px-Surrender_of_Lord_Cornwallis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Surrender_of_Lord_Cornwallis.jpg/440px-Surrender_of_Lord_Cornwallis.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Surrender_of_Lord_Cornwallis.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Surrender of Cornwallis at Yorktown</i>. The loss of the American colonies marked the end of the "first British Empire".</div></div></div>\n<p>The loss of such a large portion of <a href="/wiki/British_America" title="British America">British America</a>, at the time Britain\'s most populous overseas possession, is seen by some historians as the event defining the transition between the "first" and "second" empires,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> in which Britain shifted its attention away from the Americas to Asia, the Pacific and later Africa. <a href="/wiki/Adam_Smith" title="Adam Smith">Adam Smith</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wealth_of_Nations" title="The Wealth of Nations">Wealth of Nations</a></i>, published in 1776, had argued that colonies were redundant, and that <a href="/wiki/Free_trade" title="Free trade">free trade</a> should replace the old <a href="/wiki/Mercantilism" title="Mercantilism">mercantilist</a> policies that had characterised the first period of colonial expansion, dating back to the <a href="/wiki/Protectionism" title="Protectionism">protectionism</a> of Spain and Portugal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refpagden1_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-refpagden1-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The growth of trade between the newly independent <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and Britain after 1783 seemed to confirm Smith\'s view that political control was not necessary for economic success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The war to the south influenced British policy in Canada, where between 40,000 and 100,000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> defeated <a href="/wiki/Loyalist_(American_Revolution)" title="Loyalist (American Revolution)">Loyalists</a> had migrated from the new United States following independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The 14,000 Loyalists who went to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_John_River_(New_Brunswick)" title="Saint John River (New Brunswick)">Saint John</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Croix_River_(Maine_%E2%80%93_New_Brunswick)" title="Saint Croix River (Maine &#8211; New Brunswick)">Saint Croix river</a> valleys, then part of <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>, felt too far removed from the provincial government in Halifax, so London split off <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a> as a separate colony in 1784.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constitutional_Act_of_1791" title="Constitutional Act of 1791">Constitutional Act of 1791</a> created the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Upper_Canada" title="Upper Canada">Upper Canada</a> (mainly English-speaking) and <a href="/wiki/Lower_Canada" title="Lower Canada">Lower Canada</a> (mainly <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French-speaking</a>) to defuse tensions between the French and British communities, and implemented governmental systems similar to those employed in Britain, with the intention of asserting imperial authority and not allowing the sort of popular control of government that was perceived to have led to the American Revolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tensions between Britain and the United States escalated again during the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, as Britain tried to cut off American trade with France and boarded American ships to <a href="/wiki/Impressment" title="Impressment">impress</a> men into the Royal Navy. The US declared war, the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>, and invaded Canadian territory. In response Britain invaded the US, but the pre-war boundaries were reaffirmed by the 1814 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Ghent" title="Treaty of Ghent">Treaty of Ghent</a>, ensuring Canada\'s future would be separate from that of the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Rise_of_the_.22Second.22_British_Empire_.281783.E2.80.931815.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id=\'Rise_of_the_"Second"_British_Empire_(1783&#8211;1815)\'>Rise of the "Second" British Empire (1783&#8211;1815)</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exploration_of_the_Pacific">Exploration of the Pacific</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Captainjamescookportrait.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="1020" decoding="async" height="276" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Captainjamescookportrait.jpg/220px-Captainjamescookportrait.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Captainjamescookportrait.jpg/330px-Captainjamescookportrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Captainjamescookportrait.jpg/440px-Captainjamescookportrait.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Captainjamescookportrait.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a>\'s mission was to find the alleged southern continent <i><a href="/wiki/Terra_Australis" title="Terra Australis">Terra Australis</a></i>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Since 1718, <a href="/wiki/Penal_transportation" title="Penal transportation">transportation</a> to the American colonies had been a penalty for various offences in Britain, with approximately one thousand convicts transported per year across the Atlantic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Forced to find an alternative location after the loss of the Thirteen Colonies in 1783, the British government turned to the newly discovered lands of Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The coast of Australia had been discovered for Europeans by the Dutch explorer <a href="/wiki/Willem_Janszoon" title="Willem Janszoon">Willem Janszoon</a> in 1606 and was named <a href="/wiki/New_Holland_(Australia)" title="New Holland (Australia)">New Holland</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-81">[81]</a></sup> but there was no attempt to colonise it. In 1770 <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> discovered the eastern coast of Australia while on a scientific <a href="/wiki/First_voyage_of_James_Cook" title="First voyage of James Cook">voyage</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">South Pacific Ocean</a>, claimed the continent for Britain, and named it <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> In 1778, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Banks" title="Joseph Banks">Joseph Banks</a>, Cook\'s <a href="/wiki/Botany" title="Botany">botanist</a> on the voyage, presented evidence to the government on the suitability of <a href="/wiki/Botany_Bay" title="Botany Bay">Botany Bay</a> for the establishment of a <a href="/wiki/Penal_colony" title="Penal colony">penal settlement</a>, and in 1787 the first shipment of <a href="/wiki/Convicts_in_Australia" title="Convicts in Australia">convicts</a> set sail, arriving in 1788.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Britain continued to transport convicts to <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a> until 1840, to Tasmania until 1853 and to Western Australia until 1868.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> The Australian colonies became profitable exporters of wool and gold,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> mainly because of gold rushes in the colony of Victoria, making its capital <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a> for a time the richest city in the world<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RobertCervero320_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-RobertCervero320-86">[86]</a></sup> and the second largest city (after London) in the British Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup>\n</p><p>During his voyage, Cook also visited New Zealand, first discovered by Dutch explorer <a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">Abel Tasman</a> in 1642, and claimed the <a href="/wiki/North_Island" title="North Island">North</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Island" title="South Island">South</a> islands for the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Monarchy of the United Kingdom">British crown</a> in 1769 and 1770 respectively. Initially, interaction between the indigenous <a href="/wiki/M%C4%81ori_people" title="M&#257;ori people">M&#257;ori</a> population and Europeans was limited to the trading of goods. European settlement increased through the early decades of the 19th century, with numerous trading stations established, especially in the North. In 1839, the <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Company" title="New Zealand Company">New Zealand Company</a> announced plans to buy large tracts of land and establish colonies in New Zealand. On 6 February 1840, Captain <a href="/wiki/William_Hobson" title="William Hobson">William Hobson</a> and around 40 Maori chiefs signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Waitangi" title="Treaty of Waitangi">Treaty of Waitangi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> This treaty is considered by many to be New Zealand\'s founding document,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> but differing interpretations of the Maori and English versions of the text<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> have meant that it continues to be a source of dispute.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="War_with_Napoleonic_France">War with Napoleonic France</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a></div>\n<p>Britain was challenged again by France under <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>, in a struggle that, unlike previous wars, represented a contest of ideologies between the two nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> It was not only Britain\'s position on the world stage that was at risk: Napoleon threatened to invade Britain itself, just as his armies had overrun many countries of <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">continental Europe</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Waterloo_1815.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="846" data-file-width="1854" decoding="async" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Battle_of_Waterloo_1815.PNG/220px-Battle_of_Waterloo_1815.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Battle_of_Waterloo_1815.PNG/330px-Battle_of_Waterloo_1815.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Battle_of_Waterloo_1815.PNG/440px-Battle_of_Waterloo_1815.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Waterloo_1815.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Waterloo" title="Battle of Waterloo">Battle of Waterloo</a> ended in the defeat of <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Napoleonic Wars were therefore ones in which Britain invested large amounts of capital and resources to win. French ports were blockaded by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>, which won a decisive victory over a Franco-Spanish fleet at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trafalgar" title="Battle of Trafalgar">Trafalgar</a> in 1805. Overseas colonies were attacked and occupied, including those of the Netherlands, which was annexed by Napoleon in 1810. France was finally defeated by a coalition of European armies in 1815.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> Britain was again the beneficiary of peace treaties: France ceded the <a href="/wiki/United_States_of_the_Ionian_Islands" title="United States of the Ionian Islands">Ionian Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malta_Protectorate" title="Malta Protectorate">Malta</a> (which it had occupied in 1797 and 1798 respectively), <a href="/wiki/British_Mauritius" title="British Mauritius">Mauritius</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tobago" title="Tobago">Tobago</a>; Spain ceded <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a>; the Netherlands <a href="/wiki/British_Guiana" title="British Guiana">Guyana</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Colony" title="Cape Colony">Cape Colony</a>. Britain returned <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>, Martinique, <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>, and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="R&#233;union">R&#233;union</a> to France, and <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a> and <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> to the Netherlands, while gaining control of <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Ceylon</a> (1795&#8211;1815).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refjames165_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-refjames165-94">[94]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Abolition_of_slavery">Abolition of slavery</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Abolitionism in the United Kingdom">Abolitionism in the United Kingdom</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Mill_Yard_-_Ten_Views_in_the_Island_of_Antigua_(1823),_plate_V_-_BL.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1241" data-file-width="1784" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/The_Mill_Yard_-_Ten_Views_in_the_Island_of_Antigua_%281823%29%2C_plate_V_-_BL.jpg/220px-The_Mill_Yard_-_Ten_Views_in_the_Island_of_Antigua_%281823%29%2C_plate_V_-_BL.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/The_Mill_Yard_-_Ten_Views_in_the_Island_of_Antigua_%281823%29%2C_plate_V_-_BL.jpg/330px-The_Mill_Yard_-_Ten_Views_in_the_Island_of_Antigua_%281823%29%2C_plate_V_-_BL.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/The_Mill_Yard_-_Ten_Views_in_the_Island_of_Antigua_%281823%29%2C_plate_V_-_BL.jpg/440px-The_Mill_Yard_-_Ten_Views_in_the_Island_of_Antigua_%281823%29%2C_plate_V_-_BL.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Mill_Yard_-_Ten_Views_in_the_Island_of_Antigua_(1823),_plate_V_-_BL.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sugar plantation in the British colony of <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a>, 1823</div></div></div>\n<p>With the advent of the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, goods produced by slavery became less important to the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Economy of the United Kingdom">British economy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Added to this was the cost of suppressing regular <a href="/wiki/Slave_rebellion" title="Slave rebellion">slave rebellions</a>. With support from the British <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Abolitionism in the United Kingdom">abolitionist</a> movement, <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Parliament</a> enacted the <a href="/wiki/Slave_Trade_Act_1807" title="Slave Trade Act 1807">Slave Trade Act</a> in 1807, which abolished the <a href="/wiki/History_of_slavery" title="History of slavery">slave trade</a> in the empire. In 1808, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_Colony" title="Sierra Leone Colony">Sierra Leone Colony</a> was designated an official British colony for freed slaves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Parliamentary reform in 1832 saw the influence of the <a href="/wiki/West_India_Committee" title="West India Committee">West India Committee</a> decline. The <a href="/wiki/Slavery_Abolition_Act_1833" title="Slavery Abolition Act 1833">Slavery Abolition Act</a>, passed the following year, abolished slavery in the British Empire on 1 August 1834, finally bringing the Empire into line with the law in the UK (with the exception of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Helena" title="St. Helena">St. Helena</a>, Ceylon and the territories administered by the East India Company, though these exclusions were later repealed). Under the Act, slaves were granted full <a href="/wiki/Emancipation" title="Emancipation">emancipation</a> after a period of four to six years of "apprenticeship".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> The British government compensated slave-owners.\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Britain.27s_imperial_century_.281815.E2.80.931914.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Britain\'s_imperial_century_(1815&#8211;1914)">Britain\'s imperial century (1815&#8211;1914)</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_British_diplomatic_history#1815&#8211;1860" title="Timeline of British diplomatic history">Timeline of British diplomatic history &#167;&#160;1815&#8211;1860</a>, <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian era</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1432" data-file-width="1815" decoding="async" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg/250px-Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg/375px-Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg/500px-Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An elaborate map of the British Empire in 1910, marked in the traditional colour for imperial British dominions on maps</div></div></div>\n<p>Between 1815 and 1914, a period referred to as Britain\'s "imperial century" by some historians,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> around 10,000,000 square miles (26,000,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) of territory and roughly 400 million people were added to the British Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Victory over Napoleon left Britain without any serious international rival, other than <a href="/wiki/The_Great_Game" title="The Great Game">Russia in Central Asia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-#refOHBEv3|Porter,_p._401_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-#refOHBEv3|Porter,_p._401-101">[101]</a></sup> Unchallenged at sea, Britain adopted the role of global policeman, a state of affairs later known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Pax_Britannica" title="Pax Britannica">Pax Britannica</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-10">[10]</a></sup> and a foreign policy of "<a href="/wiki/Splendid_isolation" title="Splendid isolation">splendid isolation</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Alongside the formal control it exerted over its own colonies, Britain\'s dominant position in world trade meant that it effectively controlled the economies of many countries, such as China, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Siam</a>, which has been described by some historians as an "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Informal_Empire" title="Informal Empire">Informal Empire</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup>\n</p><p>British imperial strength was underpinned by the <a href="/wiki/Steamboat" title="Steamboat">steamship</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Telegraphy" title="Telegraphy">telegraph</a>, new technologies invented in the second half of the 19th century, allowing
