it to control and defend the empire. By 1902, the British Empire was linked together by a network of telegraph cables, called the <a href="/wiki/All_Red_Line" title="All Red Line">All Red Line</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="East_India_Company_in_Asia">East India Company in Asia</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British Raj</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Victoria_Disraeli_cartoon.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="393" data-file-width="301" decoding="async" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Victoria_Disraeli_cartoon.jpg/170px-Victoria_Disraeli_cartoon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Victoria_Disraeli_cartoon.jpg/255px-Victoria_Disraeli_cartoon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f2/Victoria_Disraeli_cartoon.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Victoria_Disraeli_cartoon.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An 1876 political cartoon of <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Disraeli" title="Benjamin Disraeli">Benjamin Disraeli</a> (1804&#8211;1881) making <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_India" title="Emperor of India">Empress of India</a>. The caption reads "New crowns for old ones!"</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a> drove the expansion of the British Empire in Asia. The Company\'s army had first joined forces with the Royal Navy during the Seven Years\' War, and the two continued to co-operate in arenas outside India: the eviction of the French from <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> (1799),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> the capture of <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Java_(1811)" title="Invasion of Java (1811)">Java</a> from the Netherlands (1811), the acquisition of <a href="/wiki/History_of_Penang#Founding_of_penang" title="History of Penang">Penang Island</a> (1786), <a href="/wiki/Founding_of_modern_Singapore" title="Founding of modern Singapore">Singapore</a> (1819) and <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Dutch_Treaty_of_1824" title="Anglo-Dutch Treaty of 1824">Malacca</a> (1824), and the defeat of <a href="/wiki/First_Anglo-Burmese_War" title="First Anglo-Burmese War">Burma</a> (1826).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-#refOHBEv3|Porter,_p._401_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-#refOHBEv3|Porter,_p._401-101">[101]</a></sup>\n</p><p>From its base in India, the Company had also been engaged in an increasingly profitable <a href="/wiki/Opium" title="Opium">opium</a> export trade to China since the 1730s. This trade, illegal since it was outlawed by the <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing dynasty</a> in 1729, helped reverse the trade imbalances resulting from the British imports of tea, which saw large outflows of silver from Britain to China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> In 1839, the confiscation by the Chinese authorities at <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Canton</a> of 20,000 chests of opium led Britain to attack China in the <a href="/wiki/First_Opium_War" title="First Opium War">First Opium War</a>, and resulted in the seizure by Britain of <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Island" title="Hong Kong Island">Hong Kong Island</a>, at that time a minor settlement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the late 18th and early 19th centuries the British Crown began to assume an increasingly large role in the affairs of the Company. A series of Acts of Parliament were passed, including the <a href="/wiki/Regulating_Act_of_1773" title="Regulating Act of 1773">Regulating Act of 1773</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pitt%27s_India_Act" title="Pitt\'s India Act">Pitt\'s India Act</a> of 1784 and the <a href="/wiki/Charter_Act_of_1813" title="Charter Act of 1813">Charter Act of 1813</a> which regulated the Company\'s affairs and established the sovereignty of the Crown over the territories that it had acquired.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> The Company\'s eventual end was precipitated by the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Rebellion_of_1857" title="Indian Rebellion of 1857">Indian Rebellion</a> in 1857, a conflict that had begun with the mutiny of <a href="/wiki/Sepoy" title="Sepoy">sepoys</a>, Indian troops under British officers and discipline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> The rebellion took six months to suppress, with heavy loss of life on both sides. The following year the British government dissolved the Company and assumed direct control over India through the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India_Act_1858" title="Government of India Act 1858">Government of India Act 1858</a>, establishing the <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British Raj</a>, where an appointed <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_India" title="Governor-General of India">governor-general</a> administered India and <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> was crowned the <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_India" title="Emperor of India">Empress of India</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> India became the empire\'s most valuable possession, "the Jewel in the Crown", and was the most important source of Britain\'s strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown5_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brown5-111">[111]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A series of serious crop failures in the late 19th century led to <a href="/wiki/Famine_in_India" title="Famine in India">widespread famines</a> on the subcontinent in which it is estimated that over 15 million people died. The East India Company had failed to implement any coordinated policy to deal with the famines during its period of rule. Later, under direct British rule, commissions were set up after each famine to investigate the causes and implement new policies, which took until the early 1900s to have an effect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalry_with_Russia">Rivalry with Russia</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Great_Game" title="The Great Game">The Great Game</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Relief_of_the_Light_Brigade.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1056" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Relief_of_the_Light_Brigade.png/220px-Relief_of_the_Light_Brigade.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Relief_of_the_Light_Brigade.png/330px-Relief_of_the_Light_Brigade.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Relief_of_the_Light_Brigade.png/440px-Relief_of_the_Light_Brigade.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Relief_of_the_Light_Brigade.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>British cavalry charging against Russian forces at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Balaclava" title="Battle of Balaclava">Balaclava</a> in 1854</div></div></div>\n<p>During the 19th century, Britain and the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> vied to fill the power vacuums that had been left by the declining <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">Qajar dynasty</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qing_Dynasty" title="Qing Dynasty">Qing Dynasty</a>. This rivalry in Central Asia came to be known as the "<a href="/wiki/The_Great_Game" title="The Great Game">Great Game</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> As far as Britain was concerned, defeats inflicted by Russia on <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_War_(1826%E2%80%931828)" title="Russo-Persian War (1826&#8211;1828)">Persia</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1828%E2%80%931829)" title="Russo-Turkish War (1828&#8211;1829)">Turkey</a> demonstrated its imperial ambitions and capabilities and stoked fears in Britain of an overland invasion of India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> In 1839, Britain moved to pre-empt this by invading <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, but the <a href="/wiki/First_Anglo-Afghan_War" title="First Anglo-Afghan War">First Anglo-Afghan War</a> was a disaster for Britain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refjames182_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-refjames182-115">[115]</a></sup>\n</p><p>When Russia invaded the Turkish <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> in 1853, fears of Russian dominance in the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a> and Middle East led Britain and France to invade the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crimean_Peninsula" title="Crimean Peninsula">Crimean Peninsula</a> to destroy Russian naval capabilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refjames182_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-refjames182-115">[115]</a></sup> The ensuing <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War (1854&#8211;56)</a>, which involved new techniques of <a href="/wiki/Modern_warfare" title="Modern warfare">modern warfare</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> was the only <a href="/wiki/World_war" title="World war">global war</a> fought between Britain and another <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">imperial power</a> during the <i>Pax Britannica</i> and was a resounding defeat for Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refjames182_115-2"><a href="#cite_note-refjames182-115">[115]</a></sup> The situation remained unresolved in Central Asia for two more decades, with Britain annexing <a href="/wiki/Baluchistan_(Chief_Commissioner%27s_Province)" title="Baluchistan (Chief Commissioner\'s Province)">Baluchistan</a> in 1876 and Russia annexing <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kirghizia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a>. For a while it appeared that another war would be inevitable, but the two countries reached an agreement on their respective <a href="/wiki/Sphere_of_influence" title="Sphere of influence">spheres of influence</a> in the region in 1878 and on all outstanding matters in 1907 with the signing of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglo-Russian_Entente" title="Anglo-Russian Entente">Anglo-Russian Entente</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> The destruction of the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Russian_Navy" title="Imperial Russian Navy">Russian Navy</a> by the Japanese at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Port_Arthur" title="Battle of Port Arthur">Battle of Port Arthur</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Japanese_War" title="Russo-Japanese War">Russo-Japanese War</a> of 1904&#8211;05 also limited its threat to the British.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hodge47_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-hodge47-118">[118]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cape_to_Cairo">Cape to Cairo</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Punch_Rhodes_Colossus.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2681" data-file-width="2069" decoding="async" height="285" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Punch_Rhodes_Colossus.png/220px-Punch_Rhodes_Colossus.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Punch_Rhodes_Colossus.png/330px-Punch_Rhodes_Colossus.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Punch_Rhodes_Colossus.png/440px-Punch_Rhodes_Colossus.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Punch_Rhodes_Colossus.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/The_Rhodes_Colossus" title="The Rhodes Colossus">The Rhodes Colossus</a></i>&#8212;<a href="/wiki/Cecil_Rhodes" title="Cecil Rhodes">Cecil Rhodes</a> spanning "Cape to Cairo"</div></div></div>\n<p>The Dutch East India Company had founded the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Colony" title="Cape Colony">Cape Colony</a> on the southern tip of Africa in 1652 as a way station for its ships travelling to and from its colonies in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indies" title="Indies">East Indies</a>. Britain formally acquired the colony, and its large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afrikaner" title="Afrikaner">Afrikaner</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Boer" title="Boer">Boer</a>) population in 1806, having occupied it in 1795 to prevent its falling into French hands during the <a href="/wiki/Flanders_Campaign" title="Flanders Campaign">Flanders Campaign</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> British immigration began to rise after 1820, and pushed thousands of Boers, resentful of British rule, northwards to found their own&#8212;mostly short-lived&#8212;independent republics, during the <a href="/wiki/Great_Trek" title="Great Trek">Great Trek</a> of the late 1830s and early 1840s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> In the process the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voortrekkers" title="Voortrekkers">Voortrekkers</a> clashed repeatedly with the British, who had their own agenda with regard to colonial expansion in South Africa and to the various native African polities, including those of the <a href="/wiki/Sotho_people" title="Sotho people">Sotho</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Zulu_people" title="Zulu people">Zulu</a> nations. Eventually the Boers established two republics which had a longer lifespan: the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Republic" title="South African Republic">South African Republic</a> or Transvaal Republic (1852&#8211;77; 1881&#8211;1902) and the <a href="/wiki/Orange_Free_State" title="Orange Free State">Orange Free State</a> (1854&#8211;1902).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> In 1902 Britain occupied both republics, concluding a treaty with the two <a href="/wiki/Boer_Republics" title="Boer Republics">Boer Republics</a> following the <a href="/wiki/Second_Boer_War" title="Second Boer War">Second Boer War</a> (1899&#8211;1902).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1869 the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> opened under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napoleon_III_of_France" title="Napoleon III of France">Napoleon III</a>, linking the Mediterranean with the Indian Ocean. Initially the Canal was opposed by the British;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> but once opened, its strategic value was quickly recognised and became the "jugular vein of the Empire".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> In 1875, the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a> government of <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Disraeli" title="Benjamin Disraeli">Benjamin Disraeli</a> bought the indebted Egyptian ruler <a href="/wiki/Isma%27il_Pasha" title="Isma\'il Pasha">Isma\'il Pasha\'s</a> 44% shareholding in the Suez Canal for &#163;4 million (equivalent to &#163;370&#160;million in 2018). Although this did not grant outright control of the strategic waterway, it did give Britain leverage. Joint Anglo-French financial control over Egypt ended in outright British occupation in 1882.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b230&#8211;33_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b230&#8211;33-125">[125]</a></sup> The French were still majority shareholders and attempted to weaken the British position,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> but a compromise was reached with the 1888 <a href="/wiki/Convention_of_Constantinople" title="Convention of Constantinople">Convention of Constantinople</a>, which made the Canal officially neutral territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup>\n</p><p>With competitive French, <a href="/wiki/Belgian_colonial_empire" title="Belgian colonial empire">Belgian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese</a> activity in the lower <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a> region undermining orderly colonisation of tropical Africa, the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Conference" title="Berlin Conference">Berlin Conference</a> of 1884&#8211;85 was held to regulate the competition between the European powers in what was called the "<a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a>" by defining "effective occupation" as the criterion for international recognition of territorial claims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> The scramble continued into the 1890s, and caused Britain to reconsider its decision in 1885 to withdraw from <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>. A joint force of British and Egyptian troops defeated the <a href="/wiki/Mahdist_War" title="Mahdist War">Mahdist Army</a> in 1896, and rebuffed an attempted French invasion <a href="/wiki/Fashoda_Incident" title="Fashoda Incident">at Fashoda</a> in 1898. Sudan was nominally made an <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Egyptian_Sudan" title="Anglo-Egyptian Sudan">Anglo-Egyptian condominium</a>, but a British colony in reality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup>\n</p><p>British gains in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa" title="Southern Africa">Southern</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Africa" title="East Africa">East Africa</a> prompted <a href="/wiki/Cecil_Rhodes" title="Cecil Rhodes">Cecil Rhodes</a>, pioneer of British expansion in Southern Africa, to urge a "<a href="/wiki/Cape_to_Cairo_Railway" title="Cape to Cairo Railway">Cape to Cairo</a>" railway linking the strategically important <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> to the mineral-rich south of the continent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> During the 1880s and 1890s, Rhodes, with his privately owned <a href="/wiki/British_South_Africa_Company" title="British South Africa Company">British South Africa Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Company_rule_in_Rhodesia" title="Company rule in Rhodesia">occupied and annexed</a> territories subsequently named after him, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhodesia_(name)" title="Rhodesia (name)">Rhodesia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Changing_status_of_the_white_colonies">Changing status of the white colonies</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Horses_hauling_timber_Ontario.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="464" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Horses_hauling_timber_Ontario.jpg/210px-Horses_hauling_timber_Ontario.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Horses_hauling_timber_Ontario.jpg/315px-Horses_hauling_timber_Ontario.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Horses_hauling_timber_Ontario.jpg/420px-Horses_hauling_timber_Ontario.jpg 2x" width="210"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Horses_hauling_timber_Ontario.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Canada" title="Dominion of Canada">Canada</a>\'s major industry in terms of employment and value of the product was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forest_exploitation_in_canada" title="Forest exploitation in canada">timber trade</a> (Ontario, 1900 circa).</div></div></div>\n<p>The path to independence for the white colonies of the British Empire began with the 1839 <a href="/wiki/Report_on_the_Affairs_of_British_North_America" title="Report on the Affairs of British North America">Durham Report</a>, which proposed unification and self-government for <a href="/wiki/Upper_Canada" title="Upper Canada">Upper</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lower_Canada" title="Lower Canada">Lower Canada</a>, as a solution to political unrest which had erupted in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rebellions_of_1837" title="Rebellions of 1837">armed rebellions</a> in 1837.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> This began with the passing of the <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Union_1840" title="Act of Union 1840">Act of Union</a> in 1840, which created the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Canada" title="Province of Canada">Province of Canada</a>. <a href="/wiki/Responsible_government" title="Responsible government">Responsible government</a> was first granted to <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a> in 1848, and was soon extended to the other British North American colonies. With the passage of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_North_America_Act,_1867" title="British North America Act, 1867">British North America Act, 1867</a> by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Parliament" title="British Parliament">British Parliament</a>, Upper and Lower Canada, New Brunswick and Nova Scotia were formed into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Canada" title="Dominion of Canada">Dominion of Canada</a>, a confederation enjoying full self-government with the exception of <a href="/wiki/International_relations" title="International relations">international relations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Australia and New Zealand achieved similar levels of self-government after 1900, with the Australian colonies <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Australia" title="Federation of Australia">federating in 1901</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> The term "dominion status" was officially introduced at the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Conference" title="Imperial Conference">Colonial Conference of 1907</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rhodes5_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-rhodes5-135">[135]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The last decades of the 19th century saw concerted <a href="/wiki/Political_campaign" title="Political campaign">political campaigns</a> for Irish <a href="/wiki/Home_rule" title="Home rule">home rule</a>. Ireland had been united with Britain into the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Act_of_Union_1800" title="Act of Union 1800">Act of Union 1800</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Rebellion_of_1798" title="Irish Rebellion of 1798">Irish Rebellion of 1798</a>, and had suffered a severe <a href="/wiki/Great_Famine_(Ireland)" title="Great Famine (Ireland)">famine</a> between 1845 and 1852. Home rule was supported by the British <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Ewart_Gladstone" title="William Ewart Gladstone">William Gladstone</a>, who hoped that Ireland might follow in Canada\'s footsteps as a Dominion within the empire, but his 1886 <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ireland_Bill_1886" title="Government of Ireland Bill 1886">Home Rule bill</a> was defeated in Parliament. Although the bill, if passed, would have granted Ireland less autonomy within the UK than the Canadian provinces had within their own federation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> many MPs feared that a partially independent Ireland might pose a security threat to Great Britain or mark the beginning of the break-up of the empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-James,_p._315_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-James,_p._315-137">[137]</a></sup> A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_Government_Bill_1893" title="Irish Government Bill 1893">second Home Rule bill</a> was also defeated for similar reasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-James,_p._315_137-1"><a href="#cite_note-James,_p._315-137">[137]</a></sup> A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Home_Rule_Act_1914" title="Home Rule Act 1914">third bill</a> was passed by Parliament in 1914, but not implemented because of the outbreak of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_World_War" title="First World War">First World War</a> leading to the 1916 <a href="/wiki/Easter_Rising" title="Easter Rising">Easter Rising</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="World_wars_.281914.E2.80.931945.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="World_wars_(1914&#8211;1945)">World wars (1914&#8211;1945)</span></h2>\n<p>By the turn of the 20th century, fears had begun to grow in Britain that it would no longer be able to defend the <a href="/wiki/Metropole" title="Metropole">metropole</a> and the entirety of the empire while at the same time maintaining the policy of "<a href="/wiki/Splendid_isolation" title="Splendid isolation">splendid isolation</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Germany was rapidly rising as a military and industrial power and was now seen as the most likely opponent in any future war. Recognising that it was overstretched in the Pacific<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> and threatened at home by the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_German_Navy" title="Imperial German Navy">Imperial German Navy</a>, Britain <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Japanese_Alliance" title="Anglo-Japanese Alliance">formed an alliance with Japan</a> in 1902 and with its old enemies <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Entente_cordiale" title="Entente cordiale">France</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglo-Russian_Entente" title="Anglo-Russian Entente">Russia</a> in 1904 and 1907, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_World_War">First World War</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_Kingdom_during_the_First_World_War" title="History of the United Kingdom during the First World War">History of the United Kingdom during the First World War</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Australian_53rd_Bn_Fromelles_19_July_1916.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="584" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="277" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Australian_53rd_Bn_Fromelles_19_July_1916.jpg/190px-Australian_53rd_Bn_Fromelles_19_July_1916.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Australian_53rd_Bn_Fromelles_19_July_1916.jpg/285px-Australian_53rd_Bn_Fromelles_19_July_1916.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Australian_53rd_Bn_Fromelles_19_July_1916.jpg/380px-Australian_53rd_Bn_Fromelles_19_July_1916.jpg 2x" width="190"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Australian_53rd_Bn_Fromelles_19_July_1916.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Soldiers of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australian_5th_Division" title="Australian 5th Division">Australian 5th Division</a>, waiting to attack during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fromelles" title="Battle of Fromelles">Battle of Fromelles</a>, 19 July 1916</div></div></div>\n<p>Britain\'s fears of war with Germany were realised in 1914 with the outbreak of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_World_War" title="First World War">First World War</a>. Britain quickly invaded and occupied most of Germany\'s overseas colonies in Africa. In the Pacific, Australia and New Zealand occupied <a href="/wiki/German_New_Guinea" title="German New Guinea">German New Guinea</a> and <a href="/wiki/German_Samoa" title="German Samoa">German Samoa</a> respectively. Plans for a post-war division of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, which had joined the war on Germany\'s side, were secretly drawn up by Britain and France under the 1916 <a href="/wiki/Sykes%E2%80%93Picot_Agreement" title="Sykes&#8211;Picot Agreement">Sykes&#8211;Picot Agreement</a>. This agreement was not divulged to the <a href="/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_Sharif_of_Mecca" title="Hussein bin Ali, Sharif of Mecca">Sharif of Mecca</a>, who the British had been encouraging to launch an Arab revolt against their Ottoman rulers, giving the impression that Britain was supporting the creation of an independent Arab state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown494-495_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brown494-495-142">[142]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Empire_Needs_Men_WWI.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="407" decoding="async" height="280" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/The_Empire_Needs_Men_WWI.jpg/190px-The_Empire_Needs_Men_WWI.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/The_Empire_Needs_Men_WWI.jpg/285px-The_Empire_Needs_Men_WWI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/The_Empire_Needs_Men_WWI.jpg/380px-The_Empire_Needs_Men_WWI.jpg 2x" width="190"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Empire_Needs_Men_WWI.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A poster urging men from countries of the British Empire to enlist in the British Army</div></div></div>\n<p>The British declaration of war on Germany and its allies also committed the colonies and Dominions, which provided invaluable military, financial and material support. Over 2.5 million men served in the armies of the <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">Dominions</a>, as well as many thousands of volunteers from the <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">Crown colonies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> The contributions of Australian and New Zealand troops during the 1915 <a href="/wiki/Gallipoli_Campaign" title="Gallipoli Campaign">Gallipoli Campaign</a> against the Ottoman Empire had a great impact on the national consciousness at home, and marked a watershed in the transition of Australia and New Zealand from colonies to nations in their own right. The countries continue to commemorate this occasion on <a href="/wiki/Anzac_Day" title="Anzac Day">Anzac Day</a>. Canadians viewed the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vimy_Ridge" title="Battle of Vimy Ridge">Battle of Vimy Ridge</a> in a similar light.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> The important contribution of the Dominions to the <a href="/wiki/War_effort" title="War effort">war effort</a> was recognised in 1917 by the British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/David_Lloyd_George" title="David Lloyd George">David Lloyd George</a> when he invited each of the Dominion Prime Ministers to join an <a href="/wiki/Imperial_War_Cabinet" title="Imperial War Cabinet">Imperial War Cabinet</a> to co-ordinate imperial policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Under the terms of the concluding <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a> signed in 1919, the empire reached its greatest extent with the addition of 1,800,000 square miles (4,700,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) and 13 million new subjects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b315_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b315-146">[146]</a></sup> The colonies of Germany and the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> were distributed to the Allied powers as <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">League of Nations mandates</a>. Britain gained control of <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">Palestine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Transjordan" title="Emirate of Transjordan">Transjordan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Iraq_(Mandate_administration)" title="Kingdom of Iraq (Mandate administration)">Iraq</a>, parts of <a href="/wiki/British_Cameroons" title="British Cameroons">Cameroon</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Togoland" title="British Togoland">Togoland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tanganyika_(territory)" title="Tanganyika (territory)">Tanganyika</a>. The Dominions themselves also acquired mandates of their own: the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_Africa" title="Union of South Africa">Union of South Africa</a> gained <a href="/wiki/South_West_Africa" title="South West Africa">South West Africa</a> (modern-day <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a>), Australia gained <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_New_Guinea" title="Territory of New Guinea">New Guinea</a>, and New Zealand <a href="/wiki/Western_Samoa_Trust_Territory" title="Western Samoa Trust Territory">Western Samoa</a>. <a href="/wiki/History_of_Nauru#World_War_I_to_World_War_II" title="History of Nauru">Nauru</a> was made a combined mandate of Britain and the two Pacific Dominions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inter-war_period">Inter-war period</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:British_Empire_1921.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1425" decoding="async" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/British_Empire_1921.png/400px-British_Empire_1921.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/British_Empire_1921.png/600px-British_Empire_1921.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/British_Empire_1921.png/800px-British_Empire_1921.png 2x" width="400"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:British_Empire_1921.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>British Empire at its territorial peak in 1921</div></div></div>\n<p>The changing world order that the war had brought about, in particular the growth of the United States and Japan as naval powers, and the rise of independence movements in India and Ireland, caused a major reassessment of British imperial policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> Forced to choose between alignment with the United States or Japan, Britain opted not to renew its Japanese alliance and instead signed the 1922 <a href="/wiki/Washington_Naval_Treaty" title="Washington Naval Treaty">Washington Naval Treaty</a>, where Britain accepted naval parity with the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reflouis302_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-reflouis302-149">[149]</a></sup> This decision was the source of much debate in Britain during the 1930s<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> as militaristic governments took hold in Germany and Japan helped in part by the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, for it was feared that the empire could not survive a simultaneous attack by both nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> The issue of the empire\'s security was a serious concern in Britain, as it was vital to the British economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1919, the frustrations caused by delays to <a href="/wiki/Irish_Home_Rule_movement" title="Irish Home Rule movement">Irish home rule</a> led the MPs of <a href="/wiki/Sinn_F%C3%A9in" title="Sinn F&#233;in">Sinn F&#233;in</a>, a pro-independence party that had won a majority of the Irish seats in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_general_election,_1918" title="Irish general election, 1918">1918 British general election</a>, to establish an <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1il_%C3%89ireann_(Irish_Republic)" title="D&#225;il &#201;ireann (Irish Republic)">independent parliament</a> in Dublin, at which <a href="/wiki/Irish_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Irish Declaration of Independence">Irish independence was declared</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Irish_Republican_Army" title="Irish Republican Army">Irish Republican Army</a> simultaneously began a <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">guerrilla war</a> against the British administration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Irish_War_of_Independence" title="Irish War of Independence">Anglo-Irish War</a> ended in 1921 with a stalemate and the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Irish_Treaty" title="Anglo-Irish Treaty">Anglo-Irish Treaty</a>, creating the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a>, a Dominion within the British Empire, with effective internal independence but still constitutionally linked with the British Crown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, consisting of six of the 32 <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Ireland" title="Counties of Ireland">Irish counties</a> which had been established as a devolved region under the 1920 <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ireland_Act_1920" title="Government of Ireland Act 1920">Government of Ireland Act</a>, immediately exercised its option under the treaty to retain its existing status within the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ImperialConference.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="507" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/ImperialConference.jpg/220px-ImperialConference.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/ImperialConference.jpg/330px-ImperialConference.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/ImperialConference.jpg/440px-ImperialConference.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ImperialConference.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/George_V" title="George V">George V</a> with the British and Dominion prime ministers at the <a href="/wiki/1926_Imperial_Conference" title="1926 Imperial Conference">1926 Imperial Conference</a></div></div></div>\n<p>A similar struggle began in India when the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India_Act_1919" title="Government of India Act 1919">Government of India Act 1919</a> failed to satisfy demand for independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b330_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b330-156">[156]</a></sup> Concerns over communist and foreign plots following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ghadar_Conspiracy" title="Ghadar Conspiracy">Ghadar Conspiracy</a> ensured that war-time strictures were renewed by the <a href="/wiki/Rowlatt_Act" title="Rowlatt Act">Rowlatt Acts</a>. This led to tension,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refjames416_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-refjames416-157">[157]</a></sup> particularly in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Punjab_region" title="Punjab region">Punjab region</a>, where repressive measures culminated in the <a href="/wiki/Jallianwala_Bagh_massacre" title="Jallianwala Bagh massacre">Amritsar Massacre</a>. In Britain public opinion was divided over the morality of the massacre, between those who saw it as having saved India from anarchy, and those who viewed it with revulsion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refjames416_157-1"><a href="#cite_note-refjames416-157">[157]</a></sup> The subsequent <a href="/wiki/Non-cooperation_movement" title="Non-cooperation movement">Non-Co-Operation movement</a> was called off in March 1922 following the <a href="/wiki/Chauri_Chaura_incident" title="Chauri Chaura incident">Chauri Chaura incident</a>, and discontent continued to simmer for the next 25 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1922, Egypt, which had been declared a British <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorate</a> at the outbreak of the First World War, was <a href="/wiki/Unilateral_Declaration_of_Egyptian_Independence" title="Unilateral Declaration of Egyptian Independence">granted formal independence</a>, though it continued to be a British <a href="/wiki/Client_state" title="Client state">client state</a> until 1954. <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British troops</a> remained stationed in Egypt until the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Egyptian_treaty_of_1936" title="Anglo-Egyptian treaty of 1936">Anglo-Egyptian Treaty</a> in 1936,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> under which it was agreed that the troops would withdraw but continue to occupy and defend the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> zone. In return, Egypt was assisted in joining the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Iraq_(Mandate_administration)" title="Kingdom of Iraq (Mandate administration)">Iraq</a>, a British <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">mandate</a> since 1920, also gained membership of the League in its own right after achieving independence from Britain in 1932.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">Palestine</a>, Britain was presented with the problem of mediating between the Arabs and increasing numbers of Jews. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1917_Balfour_Declaration" title="1917 Balfour Declaration">1917 Balfour Declaration</a>, which had been incorporated into the terms of the mandate, stated that a national home for the Jewish people would be established in Palestine, and Jewish immigration allowed up to a limit that would be determined by the mandatory power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> This led to increasing conflict with the Arab population, who openly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1936%E2%80%9339_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine" title="1936&#8211;39 Arab revolt in Palestine">revolted in 1936</a>. As the threat of war with Germany increased during the 1930s, Britain judged the support of Arabs as more important than the establishment of a Jewish homeland, and shifted to a pro-Arab stance, limiting Jewish immigration and in turn triggering a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_insurgency_in_Palestine" title="Jewish insurgency in Palestine">Jewish insurgency</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown494-495_142-1"><a href="#cite_note-Brown494-495-142">[142]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The right of the Dominions to set their own foreign policy, independent of Britain, was recognised at the <a href="/wiki/1923_Imperial_Conference" title="1923 Imperial Conference">1923 Imperial Conference</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> Britain\'s request for military assistance from the Dominions at the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Chanak_Crisis" title="Chanak Crisis">Chanak Crisis</a> the previous year had been turned down by Canada and South Africa, and Canada had refused to be bound by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lausanne_(1923)" title="Treaty of Lausanne (1923)">Treaty of Lausanne (1923)</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> After pressure from the Irish Free State and South Africa, the <a href="/wiki/1926_Imperial_Conference" title="1926 Imperial Conference">1926 Imperial Conference</a> issued the <a href="/wiki/Balfour_Declaration_of_1926" title="Balfour Declaration of 1926">Balfour Declaration of 1926</a>, declaring the Dominions to be "autonomous Communities within the British Empire, equal in status, in no way subordinate one to another" within a "British <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> This declaration was given legal substance under the 1931 <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Westminster_1931" title="Statute of Westminster 1931">Statute of Westminster</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rhodes5_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-rhodes5-135">[135]</a></sup> The parliaments of Canada, Australia, New Zealand, the Union of South Africa, the Irish Free State and <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Newfoundland" title="Dominion of Newfoundland">Newfoundland</a> were now independent of British legislative control, they could nullify <a href="/wiki/Law_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Law of the United Kingdom">British laws</a> and Britain could no longer pass laws for them without their consent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> Newfoundland reverted to colonial status in 1933, suffering from financial difficulties during the Great Depression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> The Irish Free State distanced itself further from the British state with the introduction of a <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Ireland" title="Constitution of Ireland">new constitution</a> in 1937, making it a republic in all but name.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_World_War">Second World War</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/British_Empire_in_World_War_II" title="British Empire in World War II">British Empire in World War II</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1772" data-file-width="1784" decoding="async" height="219" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg/220px-El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg/330px-El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg/440px-El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>During the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eighth_Army_(United_Kingdom)" title="Eighth Army (United Kingdom)">Eighth Army</a> was made up of units from many different countries in the British Empire and Commonwealth; it fought in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_African_campaign" title="North African campaign">North African</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian_Campaign_(World_War_II)" title="Italian Campaign (World War II)">Italian</a> campaigns.</div></div></div>\n<p>Britain\'s declaration of war against <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> in September 1939 included the <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">Crown colonies</a> and India but did not automatically commit the Dominions of Australia, Canada, New Zealand, Newfoundland and South Africa. All soon declared war on Germany, but Ireland chose to remain <a href="/wiki/Irish_neutrality_during_World_War_II" title="Irish neutrality during World War II">legally neutral</a> throughout <a href="/wiki/The_Emergency_(Ireland)" title="The Emergency (Ireland)">the war</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_France" title="Battle of France">Fall of France</a> in June 1940, Britain and the empire stood alone against Germany, until the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_invasion_of_Greece" title="German invasion of Greece">German invasion of Greece</a> on 7 April 1941. British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> successfully lobbied President <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> for <a href="/wiki/Military_aid" title="Military aid">military aid</a> from the United States, but Roosevelt was not yet ready to ask <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">Congress</a> to commit the country to war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> In August 1941, Churchill and Roosevelt met and signed the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Charter" title="Atlantic Charter">Atlantic Charter</a>, which included the statement that "the rights of all peoples to choose the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Form_of_government" title="Form of government">form of government</a> under which they live" should be respected. This wording was ambiguous as to whether it referred to European countries invaded by Germany and Italy, or the peoples colonised by European nations, and would later be interpreted differently by the British, Americans, and nationalist movements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reflloyd316_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-reflloyd316-172">[172]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 1941, <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japan</a> launched, in quick succession, attacks on <a href="/wiki/British_Malaya" title="British Malaya">British Malaya</a>, the United States naval base at <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">Pearl Harbor</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hong_Kong" title="Battle of Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>. Churchill\'s reaction to the entry of the United States into the war was that Britain was now assured of victory and the future of the empire was safe,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> but the manner in which British forces were rapidly defeated in the Far East irreversibly harmed Britain\'s standing and prestige as an imperial power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> Most damaging of all was the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Singapore" title="Battle of Singapore">Fall of Singapore</a>, which had previously been hailed as an impregnable fortress and the eastern equivalent of Gibraltar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> The realisation that Britain could not defend its entire empire pushed Australia and New Zealand, which now appeared threatened by Japanese forces, into closer ties with the United States. This resulted in the 1951 <a href="/wiki/ANZUS" title="ANZUS">ANZUS Pact</a> between Australia, New Zealand and the United States of America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reflloyd316_172-1"><a href="#cite_note-reflloyd316-172">[172]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Decolonisation_and_decline_.281945.E2.80.931997.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Decolonisation_and_decline_(1945&#8211;1997)">Decolonisation and decline (1945&#8211;1997)</span></h2>\n<p><span id="Decline"></span>\nThough Britain and the empire emerged victorious from the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>, the effects of the conflict were profound, both at home and abroad. Much of Europe, a continent that had dominated the world for several centuries, was in ruins, and host to the armies of the United States and the Soviet Union, who now held the balance of global power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> Britain was left essentially bankrupt, with insolvency only averted in 1946 after the negotiation of <a href="/wiki/Anglo-American_loan" title="Anglo-American loan">a $US 4.33&#160;billion loan</a> from the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> the last instalment of which was repaid in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GT-DEX-2006-33_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-GT-DEX-2006-33-180">[180]</a></sup> At the same time, anti-colonial movements were on the rise in the colonies of European nations. The situation was complicated further by the increasing <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> rivalry of the United States and the Soviet Union. In principle, both nations were opposed to European colonialism. In practice, however, American <a href="/wiki/Anti-communism" title="Anti-communism">anti-communism</a> prevailed over <a href="/wiki/Anti-imperialism" title="Anti-imperialism">anti-imperialism</a>, and therefore the United States supported the continued existence of the British Empire to keep Communist expansion in check.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> The "<a href="/wiki/Wind_of_Change_(speech)" title="Wind of Change (speech)">wind of change</a>" ultimately meant that the British Empire\'s days were numbered, and on the whole, Britain adopted a policy of peaceful disengagement from its colonies once stable, non-Communist governments were available to transfer power to. This was in contrast to other European powers such as France and Portugal,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> which waged costly and ultimately unsuccessful wars to keep their empires intact. Between 1945 and 1965, the number of people under British rule outside the UK itself fell from 700 million to five million, three million of whom were in Hong Kong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Initial_disengagement">Initial disengagement</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Emergency_trains_crowded_with_desperate_refugees.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="424" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Emergency_trains_crowded_with_desperate_refugees.jpg/220px-Emergency_trains_crowded_with_desperate_refugees.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Emergency_trains_crowded_with_desperate_refugees.jpg/330px-Emergency_trains_crowded_with_desperate_refugees.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Emergency_trains_crowded_with_desperate_refugees.jpg/440px-Emergency_trains_crowded_with_desperate_refugees.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Emergency_trains_crowded_with_desperate_refugees.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>About 14.5 million people lost their homes as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_India" title="Partition of India">partition of India</a> in 1947.</div></div></div>\n<p>The pro-decolonisation <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> government, elected at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1945" title="United Kingdom general election, 1945">1945 general election</a> and led by <a href="/wiki/Clement_Attlee" title="Clement Attlee">Clement Attlee</a>, moved quickly to tackle the most pressing issue facing the empire: <a href="/wiki/Indian_independence_movement" title="Indian independence movement">Indian independence</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> India\'s two major political parties&#8212;the <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">Indian National Congress</a> (led by <a href="/wiki/Mahatma_Gandhi" title="Mahatma Gandhi">Mahatma Gandhi</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/All-India_Muslim_League" title="All-India Muslim League">Muslim League</a> (led by <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ali_Jinnah" title="Muhammad Ali Jinnah">Muhammad Ali Jinnah</a>)&#8212;had been campaigning for independence for decades, but disagreed as to how it should be implemented. Congress favoured a unified secular Indian state, whereas the League, fearing domination by the Hindu majority, desired a separate <a href="/wiki/Islamic_state" title="Islamic state">Islamic state</a> for Muslim-majority regions. Increasing <a href="/wiki/Civil_disorder" title="Civil disorder">civil unrest</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Indian_Navy_mutiny" title="Royal Indian Navy mutiny">mutiny</a> of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Indian_Navy" title="History of the Indian Navy">Royal Indian Navy</a> during 1946 led Attlee to promise independence no later than 30 June 1948. When the urgency of the situation and risk of civil war became apparent, the newly appointed (and last) Viceroy, <a href="/wiki/Louis_Mountbatten,_1st_Earl_Mountbatten_of_Burma" title="Louis Mountbatten, 1st Earl Mountbatten of Burma">Lord Mountbatten</a>, hastily brought forward the date to 15 August 1947.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> The borders drawn by the British to broadly <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_India" title="Partition of India">partition India</a> into Hindu and Muslim areas left tens of millions as minorities in the newly independent states of India and <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> Millions of Muslims subsequently crossed from India to Pakistan and Hindus vice versa, and violence between the two communities cost hundreds of thousands of lives. Burma, which had been administered as part of the <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British Raj</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> gained their independence the following year in 1948. India, Pakistan and Sri Lanka became members of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a>, while Burma chose not to join.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The British <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">mandate in Palestine</a>, where an Arab majority lived alongside a Jewish minority, presented the British with a similar problem to that of India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> The matter was complicated by large numbers of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_refugees" title="Jewish refugees">Jewish refugees</a> seeking to be admitted to Palestine following the <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">Holocaust</a>, while Arabs were opposed to the creation of a Jewish state. Frustrated by the intractability of the problem, attacks by Jewish paramilitary organisations and the increasing cost of maintaining its military presence, Britain announced in 1947 that it would withdraw in 1948 and leave the matter to the United Nations to solve.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">UN General Assembly</a> subsequently voted for a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine" title="United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine">plan to partition Palestine</a> into a Jewish and an Arab state.\n</p><p>Following the surrender of Japan in the Second World War, anti-Japanese <a href="/wiki/Resistance_movement" title="Resistance movement">resistance movements</a> in Malaya turned their attention towards the British, who had moved to quickly retake control of the colony, valuing it as a source of rubber and tin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-190">[190]</a></sup> The fact that the guerrillas were primarily Malayan-Chinese Communists meant that the British attempt to quell the uprising was supported by the Muslim Malay majority, on the understanding that once the insurgency had been quelled, independence would be granted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_190-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-190">[190]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Malayan_Emergency" title="Malayan Emergency">Malayan Emergency</a>, as it was called, began in 1948 and lasted until 1960, but by 1957, Britain felt confident enough to grant independence to the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Malaya" title="Federation of Malaya">Federation of Malaya</a> within the Commonwealth. In 1963, the 11 states of the federation together with Singapore, Sarawak and <a href="/wiki/Crown_Colony_of_North_Borneo" title="Crown Colony of North Borneo">North Borneo</a> joined to form <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, but in 1965 Chinese-majority Singapore was expelled from the union following tensions between the Malay and Chinese populations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, which had been a British protectorate since 1888, declined to join the union<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> and maintained its status until independence in 1984.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Suez_and_its_aftermath">Suez and its aftermath</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Suez_Crisis" title="Suez Crisis">Suez Crisis</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eden,_Anthony.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4458" data-file-width="3772" decoding="async" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Eden%2C_Anthony.jpg/170px-Eden%2C_Anthony.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Eden%2C_Anthony.jpg/255px-Eden%2C_Anthony.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Eden%2C_Anthony.jpg/340px-Eden%2C_Anthony.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eden,_Anthony.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Eden" title="Anthony Eden">Anthony Eden</a>\'s decision to invade <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Crisis" title="Suez Crisis">Suez Crisis</a> ended his political career and revealed Britain\'s weakness as an imperial power.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1951, the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative Party</a> returned to power in Britain, under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>. Churchill and the Conservatives believed that Britain\'s position as a world power relied on the continued existence of the empire, with the base at the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> allowing Britain to maintain its pre-eminent position in the Middle East in spite of the loss of India. However, Churchill could not ignore <a href="/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser" title="Gamal Abdel Nasser">Gamal Abdul Nasser</a>\'s new revolutionary <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Egypt" title="Politics of Egypt">government of Egypt</a> that had <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egyptian_Revolution_of_1952" title="Egyptian Revolution of 1952">taken power in 1952</a>, and the following year it was agreed that British troops would withdraw from the Suez Canal zone and that <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Egyptian_Sudan" title="Anglo-Egyptian Sudan">Sudan</a> would be granted self-determination by 1955, with independence to follow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/History_of_Sudan_(1956%E2%80%9369)" title="History of Sudan (1956&#8211;69)">Sudan</a> was granted independence on 1 January 1956.\n</p><p>In July 1956, Nasser unilaterally nationalised the Suez Canal. The response of <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Eden" title="Anthony Eden">Anthony Eden</a>, who had succeeded Churchill as Prime Minister, was to collude with France to engineer an Israeli attack on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Egypt_(1953%E2%80%9358)" title="Republic of Egypt (1953&#8211;58)">Egypt</a> that would give Britain and France an excuse to intervene militarily and retake the canal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> Eden infuriated US President <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a>, by his lack of consultation, and Eisenhower refused to back the invasion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b355_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b355-195">[195]</a></sup> Another of Eisenhower\'s concerns was the possibility of a wider war with the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> after it threatened to intervene on the Egyptian side. Eisenhower applied <a href="/wiki/Leverage_(finance)" title="Leverage (finance)">financial leverage</a> by threatening to sell US reserves of the <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">British pound</a> and thereby precipitate a collapse of the British currency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b356_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b356-196">[196]</a></sup> Though the invasion force was militarily successful in its objectives,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> UN intervention and US pressure forced Britain into a humiliating withdrawal of its forces, and Eden resigned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Suez_Crisis" title="Suez Crisis">Suez Crisis</a> very publicly exposed Britain\'s limitations to the world and confirmed Britain\'s decline on the world stage and its end as a superpower<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup>, demonstrating that henceforth it could no longer act without at least the acquiescence, if not the full support, of the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> The events at Suez wounded British <a href="/wiki/Patriotism" title="Patriotism">national pride</a>, leading one <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" title="Member of Parliament">MP</a> to describe it as "Britain\'s <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Waterloo" title="Battle of Waterloo">Waterloo</a>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-#refOHBEv4|Brown,_p._343_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-#refOHBEv4|Brown,_p._343-206">[206]</a></sup> and another to suggest that the country had become an "American <a href="/wiki/Satellite_state" title="Satellite state">satellite</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a> later described the mindset she believed had befallen Britain\'s political leaders after Suez where they "went from believing that Britain could do anything to an almost neurotic belief that Britain could do nothing", from which Britain did not recover until the successful recapture of the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> from <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> in 1982.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup>\n</p><p>While the Suez Crisis caused British power in the Middle East to weaken, it did not collapse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> Britain again deployed its armed forces to the region, intervening in <a href="/wiki/Muscat_and_Oman" title="Muscat and Oman">Oman</a> (<a href="/wiki/Jebel_Akhdar_War" title="Jebel Akhdar War">1957</a>), <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a> (<a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_127" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 127">1958</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Sheikhdom_of_Kuwait" title="Sheikhdom of Kuwait">Kuwait</a> (<a href="/wiki/Operation_Vantage" title="Operation Vantage">1961</a>), though on these occasions with American approval,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> as the new Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Harold_Macmillan" title="Harold Macmillan">Harold Macmillan</a>\'s foreign policy was to remain firmly aligned with the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-#refOHBEv4|Brown,_p._343_206-1"><a href="#cite_note-#refOHBEv4|Brown,_p._343-206">[206]</a></sup> Britain maintained a military presence in the Middle East for another decade. On 16 January 1968, a few weeks after the <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling#Bretton_Woods" title="Pound sterling">devaluation of the pound</a>, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Harold Wilson</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Defence" title="Secretary of State for Defence">Defence Secretary</a> <a href="/wiki/Denis_Healey" title="Denis Healey">Denis Healey</a> announced that British troops would be withdrawn from major military bases <a href="/wiki/East_of_Suez" title="East of Suez">East of Suez</a>, which included the ones in the Middle East, and primarily from <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> and Singapore by the end of 1971, instead of 1975 as earlier planned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> By that time over 50,000 British military personnel were still stationed in the Far East, including 30,000 in Singapore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> The British withdrew from <a href="/wiki/South_Yemen" title="South Yemen">Aden</a> in 1967, <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a> in 1971, and the <a href="/wiki/Maldives" title="Maldives">Maldives</a> in 1976.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wind_of_change">Wind of change</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Decolonisation_of_Africa" title="Decolonisation of Africa">Decolonisation of Africa</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:British_Empire_in_1959.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1425" decoding="async" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/British_Empire_in_1959.png/400px-British_Empire_in_1959.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/British_Empire_in_1959.png/600px-British_Empire_in_1959.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/British_Empire_in_1959.png/800px-British_Empire_in_1959.png 2x" width="400"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:British_Empire_in_1959.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>British Empire by 1959</div></div></div>\n<p>Macmillan gave a <a href="/wiki/Wind_of_Change_(speech)" title="Wind of Change (speech)">speech</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a>, South Africa in February 1960 where he spoke of "the wind of change blowing through this continent".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> Macmillan wished to avoid the same kind of <a href="/wiki/Algerian_War" title="Algerian War">colonial war</a> that France was fighting in <a href="/wiki/French_Algeria" title="French Algeria">Algeria</a>, and under his premiership decolonisation proceeded rapidly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> To the three colonies that had been granted independence in the 1950s&#8212;<a href="/wiki/History_of_Sudan_(1956%E2%80%9369)" title="History of Sudan (1956&#8211;69)">Sudan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_(British_colony)" title="Gold Coast (British colony)">Gold Coast</a> and <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Malaya" title="Federation of Malaya">Malaya</a>&#8212;were added nearly ten times that number during the 1960s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Britain\'s remaining colonies in Africa, except for <a href="/wiki/Self-governing_colony" title="Self-governing colony">self-governing</a> <a href="/wiki/Southern_Rhodesia" title="Southern Rhodesia">Southern Rhodesia</a>, were all granted independence by 1968. British withdrawal from the southern and eastern parts of Africa was not a peaceful process. Kenyan independence was preceded by the eight-year <a href="/wiki/Mau_Mau_Uprising" title="Mau Mau Uprising">Mau Mau Uprising</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia" title="Rhodesia">Rhodesia</a>, the 1965 <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia%27s_Unilateral_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Rhodesia\'s Unilateral Declaration of Independence">Unilateral Declaration of Independence</a> by the white minority resulted in a <a href="/wiki/Rhodesian_Bush_War" title="Rhodesian Bush War">civil war</a> that lasted until the <a href="/wiki/Lancaster_House_Agreement" title="Lancaster House Agreement">Lancaster House Agreement</a> of 1979, which set the terms for recognised independence in 1980, as the new nation of <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="2000" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png/220px-British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png/330px-British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png/440px-British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>British decolonisation in Africa. By the end of the 1960s, all but <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia" title="Rhodesia">Rhodesia</a> (the future Zimbabwe) and the South African mandate of <a href="/wiki/South_West_Africa" title="South West Africa">South West Africa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a>) had achieved recognised independence.</div></div></div>\n<p>In the Mediterranean, a guerrilla war waged by <a href="/wiki/EOKA" title="EOKA">Greek Cypriots</a> ended in 1960 leading to an independent <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, with the UK retaining the <a href="/wiki/Military_base" title="Military base">military bases</a> of <a href="/wiki/Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia" title="Akrotiri and Dhekelia">Akrotiri and Dhekelia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_in_the_Mediterranean" title="List of islands in the Mediterranean">Mediterranean islands</a> of <a href="/wiki/Malta_(island)" title="Malta (island)">Malta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gozo" title="Gozo">Gozo</a> were amicably granted independence from the UK in 1964 and became the country of <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>, though the idea had been raised in 1955 of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maltese_United_Kingdom_integration_referendum,_1956" title="Maltese United Kingdom integration referendum, 1956">integration with Britain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Most of the UK\'s <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> territories achieved independence after the departure in 1961 and 1962 of <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a> from the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a>, established in 1958 in an attempt to unite the British Caribbean colonies under one government, but which collapsed following the loss of its two largest members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-knight14_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-knight14-219">[219]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> achieved independence in 1966 and the remainder of the eastern Caribbean islands in the 1970s and 1980s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-knight14_219-1"><a href="#cite_note-knight14-219">[219]</a></sup> but <a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a> opted to revert to British rule after they had already started on the path to independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montserrat" title="Montserrat">Montserrat</a> opted to retain ties with Britain,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a> achieved independence in 1966.
