Britain\'s last colony on the American mainland, <a href="/wiki/British_Honduras" title="British Honduras">British Honduras</a>, became a <a href="/wiki/Self-governing_colony" title="Self-governing colony">self-governing colony</a> in 1964 and was renamed <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a> in 1973, achieving full independence in 1981. A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belizean-Guatemalan_territorial_dispute" title="Belizean-Guatemalan territorial dispute">dispute with Guatemala</a> over claims to Belize was left unresolved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup>\n</p><p>British territories in the Pacific acquired independence in the 1970s beginning with <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a> in 1970 and ending with <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a> in 1980. Vanuatu\'s independence was delayed because of political conflict between English and French-speaking communities, as the islands had been jointly administered as a <a href="/wiki/Condominium_(international_law)" title="Condominium (international law)">condominium</a> with France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> Fiji,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> chose to become <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realms</a>.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="End_of_empire">End of empire</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">Falklands War</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transfer_of_sovereignty_over_Hong_Kong" title="Transfer of sovereignty over Hong Kong">Transfer of sovereignty over Hong Kong</a></div>\n<p>In 1980, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Rhodesia" title="Southern Rhodesia">Southern Rhodesia</a>, Britain\'s last African colony, became the independent nation of Zimbabwe. The <a href="/wiki/New_Hebrides" title="New Hebrides">New Hebrides</a> achieved independence (as Vanuatu) in 1980, with Belize following suit in 1981. The passage of the <a href="/wiki/British_Nationality_Act_1981" title="British Nationality Act 1981">British Nationality Act 1981</a>, which reclassified the remaining Crown colonies as "British Dependent Territories" (renamed <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territories</a> in 2002)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> meant that, aside from a scattering of islands and outposts, the process of decolonisation that had begun after the Second World War was largely complete. In 1982, Britain\'s resolve in defending its remaining overseas territories was tested when <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">invaded</a> the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a>, acting on a long-standing claim that dated back to the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> Britain\'s ultimately successful military response to retake the islands during the ensuing <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">Falklands War</a> was viewed by many to have contributed to reversing the downward trend in Britain\'s status as a world power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup> The same year, the Canadian government severed its last legal link with Britain by <a href="/wiki/Patriation" title="Patriation">patriating</a> the Canadian constitution from Britain. The <a href="/wiki/Canada_Act_1982" title="Canada Act 1982">1982 Canada Act</a> passed by the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">British parliament</a> ended the need for British involvement in changes to the Canadian constitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refohbev594_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-refohbev594-19">[19]</a></sup> Similarly, the <a href="/wiki/Australia_Act_1986" title="Australia Act 1986">Australia Act 1986</a> (effective 3 March 1986) severed the constitutional link between Britain and the Australian states, while <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Constitution_Act_1986" title="Constitution Act 1986">Constitution Act 1986</a> (effective 1 January 1987) reformed the constitution of <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> to sever its constitutional link with Britain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> In 1984, <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, Britain\'s last remaining Asian protectorate, gained its independence.\n</p><p>In September 1982 the Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a>, travelled to Beijing to negotiate with the Chinese government, on the future of Britain\'s last major and most populous overseas territory, Hong Kong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> Under the terms of the 1842 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Nanking" title="Treaty of Nanking">Treaty of Nanking</a> and 1860 <a href="/wiki/Convention_of_Peking" title="Convention of Peking">Convention of Peking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Island" title="Hong Kong Island">Hong Kong Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kowloon_Peninsula" title="Kowloon Peninsula">Kowloon Peninsula</a> had been respectively ceded to Britain <i>in perpetuity</i>, but the vast majority of the colony was constituted by the <a href="/wiki/New_Territories" title="New Territories">New Territories</a>, which had been acquired under a <a href="/wiki/Convention_for_the_Extension_of_Hong_Kong_Territory" title="Convention for the Extension of Hong Kong Territory">99-year lease in 1898</a>, due to expire in 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup> Thatcher, seeing parallels with the Falkland Islands, initially wished to hold Hong Kong and proposed British administration with Chinese sovereignty, though this was rejected by China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> A deal was reached in 1984&#8212;under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Sino-British_Joint_Declaration" title="Sino-British Joint Declaration">Sino-British Joint Declaration</a>, Hong Kong would become a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_administrative_region_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Special administrative region of the People\'s Republic of China">special administrative region of the People\'s Republic of China</a>, maintaining its way of life for at least 50 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_handover_ceremony" title="Hong Kong handover ceremony">handover ceremony</a> in 1997 marked for many,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brendon-Empire-end_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Brendon-Empire-end-17">[17]</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/Charles,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Charles, Prince of Wales">Charles, Prince of Wales</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prince-Charles-Empire-End_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Prince-Charles-Empire-End-18">[18]</a></sup> who was in attendance, "the end of Empire".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refohbev594_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-refohbev594-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC-Empire-End_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-Empire-End-20">[20]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Location_of_the_BOTs.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="433" data-file-width="735" decoding="async" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Location_of_the_BOTs.svg/220px-Location_of_the_BOTs.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Location_of_the_BOTs.svg/330px-Location_of_the_BOTs.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Location_of_the_BOTs.svg/440px-Location_of_the_BOTs.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Location_of_the_BOTs.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The fourteen <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territories</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Britain retains sovereignty over 14 territories outside the British Isles, which were renamed the <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territories</a> in 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FAC_235-0"><a href="#cite_note-FAC-235">[235]</a></sup> Three are uninhabited except for transient military or scientific personnel;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FAC_235-1"><a href="#cite_note-FAC-235">[235]</a></sup> the remaining eleven are self-governing to varying degrees and are reliant on the UK for <a href="/wiki/Diplomacy" title="Diplomacy">foreign relations</a> and defence. The British government has stated its willingness to assist any Overseas Territory that wishes to proceed to independence, where that is an option,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup> and three territories have specifically voted to remain under British sovereignty (<a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bermudan_independence_referendum,_1995" title="Bermudan independence referendum, 1995">1995</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gibraltar_sovereignty_referendum,_2002" title="Gibraltar sovereignty referendum, 2002">2002</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands_sovereignty_referendum,_2013" title="Falkland Islands sovereignty referendum, 2013">2013</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Independent_results_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-Independent_results-237">[237]</a></sup>\n</p><p>British sovereignty of several of the overseas territories is disputed by their geographical neighbours: <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> is claimed by Spain, the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands" title="South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands">South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands</a> are claimed by <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_Ocean_Territory" title="British Indian Ocean Territory">British Indian Ocean Territory</a> is claimed by <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/British_Antarctic_Territory" title="British Antarctic Territory">British Antarctic Territory</a> is subject to overlapping claims by Argentina and <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, while many countries do not recognise any territorial claims in Antarctica.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Most former British colonies and protectorates are among the 52 member states of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, a non-political, <a href="/wiki/Voluntary_association" title="Voluntary association">voluntary association</a> of equal members, comprising a population of around 2.2 billion people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup> Sixteen <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realms</a> voluntarily continue to share the British monarch, Queen Elizabeth II, as their head of state. These sixteen nations are distinct and equal legal entities&#160;&#8211; the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Monarchy of the United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Australia" title="Monarchy of Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Canada" title="Monarchy of Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_New_Zealand" title="Monarchy of New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Monarchy of Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_Bahamas" title="Monarchy of the Bahamas">The Bahamas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Barbados" title="Monarchy of Barbados">Barbados</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Belize" title="Monarchy of Belize">Belize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Grenada" title="Monarchy of Grenada">Grenada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Jamaica" title="Monarchy of Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Monarchy of Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Monarchy of Saint Kitts and Nevis">Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Saint_Lucia" title="Monarchy of Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Monarchy of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_Solomon_Islands" title="Monarchy of the Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Tuvalu" title="Monarchy of Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parliament_House_at_dusk,_Canberra_ACT.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3670" data-file-width="5505" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Parliament_House_at_dusk%2C_Canberra_ACT.jpg/220px-Parliament_House_at_dusk%2C_Canberra_ACT.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Parliament_House_at_dusk%2C_Canberra_ACT.jpg/330px-Parliament_House_at_dusk%2C_Canberra_ACT.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Parliament_House_at_dusk%2C_Canberra_ACT.jpg/440px-Parliament_House_at_dusk%2C_Canberra_ACT.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Parliament_House_at_dusk,_Canberra_ACT.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Parliament House in Canberra, Australia. Britain\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Westminster_System" title="Westminster System">Westminster System</a> of governance has left a legacy of parliamentary democracies in many former colonies.</div></div></div>\n<p>Decades, and in some cases centuries, of British rule and emigration have left their mark on the independent nations that arose from the British Empire. The empire established the use of English in regions around the world. Today it is the primary language of up to 460 million people and is spoken by about one and a half billion as a first, second or foreign language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The spread of English from the latter half of the 20th century has been helped in part by the cultural and economic influence of the United States, itself originally formed from British colonies. Except in Africa where nearly all the former colonies have adopted the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential system</a>, the English <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary system</a> has served as the template for the governments for many former colonies, and <a href="/wiki/English_law" title="English law">English common law</a> for legal systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b307_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2004b307-243">[243]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%9F%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%9F%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BE_%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D_%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B3%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%81.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1294" data-file-width="1194" decoding="async" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%9F%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%9F%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BE_%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D_%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B3%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%81.jpg/170px-%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%9F%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%9F%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BE_%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D_%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B3%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%81.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%9F%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%9F%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BE_%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D_%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B3%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%81.jpg/255px-%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%9F%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%9F%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BE_%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D_%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B3%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%81.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%9F%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%9F%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BE_%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D_%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B3%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%81.jpg/340px-%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%9F%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%9F%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BE_%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D_%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B3%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%81.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%9F%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%9F%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BE_%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%B1%E0%B5%8D_%E0%B4%95%E0%B4%B3%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%81%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%A8%E0%B5%81.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">Cricket</a> being played in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>. British sports continue to be supported in various parts of the former empire.</div></div></div>\n<p>The British <a href="/wiki/Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council" title="Judicial Committee of the Privy Council">Judicial Committee of the Privy Council</a> still serves as the highest court of appeal for several former colonies in the Caribbean and Pacific. British <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionaries</a> who travelled around the globe often in advance of soldiers and civil servants spread <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglicanism</a>) to all continents. The British Empire provided refuge for religiously persecuted <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">continental Europeans</a> for hundreds of years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup> British colonial architecture, such as in churches, railway stations and government buildings, can be seen in many cities that were once part of the British Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Individual and team sports developed in Britain &#8212; particularly <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">rugby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netball" title="Netball">netball</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lawn_bowls" title="Lawn bowls">lawn bowls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hockey" title="Hockey">hockey</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lawn_tennis" title="Lawn tennis">lawn tennis</a> &#8212; were also exported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup> The British choice of system of measurement, the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_units" title="Imperial units">imperial system</a>, continues to be used in some countries in various ways. The convention of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Right-_and_left-hand_traffic" title="Right- and left-hand traffic">driving on the left hand side of the road</a> has been retained in much of the former empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Political boundaries drawn by the British did not always reflect homogeneous ethnicities or religions, contributing to conflicts in formerly colonised areas. The British Empire was also responsible for large migrations of peoples. Millions left the British Isles, with the founding settler populations of the United States, Canada, Australia and New Zealand coming mainly from Britain and Ireland. Tensions remain between the white settler populations of these countries and their indigenous minorities, and between white settler minorities and indigenous majorities in South Africa and Zimbabwe. Settlers in <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a> from Great Britain have left their mark in the form of divided <a href="/wiki/Irish_nationalism" title="Irish nationalism">nationalist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Unionism_in_Ireland" title="Unionism in Ireland">unionist</a> communities in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>. Millions of people moved to and from British colonies, with large numbers of <a href="/wiki/Non-resident_Indian_and_person_of_Indian_origin" title="Non-resident Indian and person of Indian origin">Indians</a> emigrating to other parts of the empire, such as <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a>, and Chinese people to Malaysia, Singapore and the Caribbean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup> The demographics of Britain itself were changed after the Second World War owing to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_Kingdom_since_1922#Post-war_immigration_(1945&#8211;1983)" title="Immigration to the United Kingdom since 1922">immigration to Britain</a> from its former colonies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<div
